Procedures for the Control Yuan to Impeach Officials

Control Commissioners’ Offices to Be Established in Each Region

People Filing Complaints Must Provide Guarantors

Impeachments by Control Commissioners Must Be Reviewed

The list of members of the Control Yuan has been approved by the Central Political Council and publicly announced by the State Council. The following is an exploration of the procedures for various facilities and accusations and impeachments after the establishment of the Yuan.

The country is divided into several regions. After the establishment of the Control Yuan, following the example of the imperial censors of the Qing Dynasty, the country will be divided into several regions, not necessarily based on provinces as the unit. The standard should be based on the prosperity of each province, either with one province as one region or two or three provinces combined into one region. Each region will have a Control Commissioner, appointed by the National Government upon the recommendation of the Yuan President. Control Commissioners may also serve concurrently as members of the Control Yuan. Each region will establish a Control Commissioner's Office. Although the Commissioner's Office will be their base of operations, they must periodically tour the region. The detailed draft of the above has been drafted by a committee established by the Yuan. After all members have taken office, further detailed discussions will be held, and then it will be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review and promulgated by the National Government.

Investigation is paramount for impeaching officials. The duties of the Control Yuan are, firstly, to initiate impeachments by the Control Commissioners and, secondly, to receive complaints from the people to the Control Yuan. The detailed procedures are still being drafted. The content is that people who accuse officials must have two or more reputable business guarantors. The reasons for the accusation must state the facts in detail. After the complaint is submitted, the President of the Yuan will review it and designate three Control Commissioners to conduct a joint review. The responsibility of the review is to investigate the evidence on the ground. If the results are deemed conclusive, an impeachment will be filed at the General Assembly. After being approved by the General Assembly, the Yuan will submit it to the Committee on Disciplinary Sanctions for Officials for execution. If the Control Commissioners initiate the impeachment on their own, that is, the Control Commissioners investigate officials and believe they should be impeached, they will list the evidence, or have three Control Commissioners jointly sign the proposal, and submit it to the President of the Yuan. The President of the Yuan will then send it to another three Control Commissioners for joint review. The subsequent procedures are the same as above.

People's Accusations Are Absolutely Confidential. Regardless of whether the charges against the accused officials are proven, the Control Yuan will not issue any instructions to the accusers and will maintain absolute confidentiality. In other words, the accusers are directly responsible to the Control Yuan. When the Control Yuan accepts the complaint and initiates an impeachment, the impeaching Control Commissioners are directly responsible to the accused, while the accusers and the accused never have a direct relationship.

Five Measures to Punish Officials. When the Committee on Disciplinary Sanctions for Officials accepts the Control Yuan's charges against officials, the Committee will discuss and determine, according to the law, the punishment the accused should receive, which is divided into (1) dismissal, (2) demotion, (3) salary reduction, (4) demerit, and (5) warning. When the Committee on Disciplinary Sanctions for Officials determines the charges, it will send them for execution. Except for specially appointed officials who are sent to the National Government for execution, the rest will be sent to the responsible superiors for execution within a specified period. If the accused has committed bribery and should be subject to criminal penalties, the Committee will send them to the court for execution according to legal procedures.

Sun Lianzhong's Troops Stop Entering Jiangxi

Ordered by the Central Government to Temporarily Postpone Departure

Prepared Troop Trains Have Been Returned

Jinan Correspondence: The 26th Route Army of Sun Lianzhong was ordered to enter Jiangxi, and repeated announcements were made about their departure, but it has not happened yet. On the 11th, a telegram from Jining was received here, stating that it was widely rumored in Jining that Sun's army had stopped its departure and would not enter Jiangxi for the time being. However, as there was no concrete evidence and Sun's army was quite busy preparing for departure, and issued a mobilization order on the 9th to depart on the 10th, the claim that the departure had been stopped was initially difficult to believe. However, at noon on the 10th, according to news from the 26th Route Army Headquarters, it was learned that the unit had received a telegram from the Central Government on the evening of the 10th, approving the temporary postponement of departure and the cessation of entry into Jiangxi. Therefore, the empty trains parked at Jining Station of the Jinpu Railway, intended for transporting Sun's army, were also ordered by the Railway Bureau to be completely returned starting on the 11th. According to news from the Jinan transportation sector, the Jinan Vehicle Section of the Jinpu Railway Administration received a telegram from the Vehicle Department of the General Bureau, ordering that all empty trains transporting Sun's army be returned to the southern section. The Jinan Section has telegraphed Jining Station to comply. It is reported that they were returned separately in the afternoon of the 11th, leaving only one train in Jinan to be used for loading goods and then heading south, to avoid running empty. (11th)

Perilous Situation of Ice Flooding in the Yellow River

Downstream Situation is Particularly Dangerous

Jinan Correspondence: The ice flooding of the Yellow River in this province, due to the sudden changes in temperature, with the river ice either freezing or melting, has caused dangerous conditions, as reported in previous correspondence. Zhang Lianjia, Director of the Shandong River Affairs Bureau, inspected Wang Wangzhuang in the Putai area on the 11th. The water level downstream was eight zhang and two chi above sea level, three chi higher than the major flood last year. The current water level situation has no fixed standard, because the river freezes from the sea mouth and extends upstream for two hundred li, and in the middle of this section, it is still either frozen or melted. The melted areas have accumulated ice, causing high water levels. Normally, Luokou is used as the standard, but now Luokou has lost its standard. The water level downstream is eight zhang and two chi, so the level at Luokou must be even higher. If the level at Luokou reaches nine zhang and six chi, it will reach the danger line. Although the level at Luokou has not yet reached this number, it has indeed reached a dangerous level as measured downstream. However, the dangerous areas are likely to be in the downstream area. The following is a true telegram sent by Zhang Lianjia from Putai to show the danger: Telegram from Zhang Lianjia to Han Jun, Chairman of the Provincial Government: Assuming you are aware of the Yiyou telegram. The water level at Tizi Dam dropped by one chi and two cun this morning, but the water level has risen in the area from Tuzaojia to Wang Wangzhuang downstream. The river is now full of ice floes and is freezing again. People crossing the river can now wade across the ice. With the continuous cold weather, it is unlikely to thaw soon. However, in the downstream section, which is about two hundred li long, the river water has risen out of the channel, ranging from two chi to five chi below the top of the dyke. If the ice thaws and the water level rises again, the situation will be dangerous everywhere and beyond imagination. The only plan for now is to order the villagers along both banks of the river to urgently repair the sections of the dyke that are lower than the water level, building two-chi-high subsidiary embankments as a preventive measure. In addition to ordering the concerned sections and notifying the counties of Lijin, Binxian, Putai, Qingcheng, Huimin, and Qidong, I urge you to order the above counties to take immediate action to strengthen the defenses. This would be a great act of benevolence. Zhang Lianjia respectfully Kouchong.

Situation of the Northern Section of the Pinghan Railway

Ping Correspondence: After the Central Government sent He Jingwu to Ping to take over the Pinghan Railway Bureau, it moved the bureau to Hankou, but still established an office in Ping. Recently, the Director of the office, Ge Li, discussed the situation of the northern section in detail, summarized as follows:

Restoring Train Service: Before the unification of railway administration, the ordinary trains on the northern section of the Pinghan Railway only ran to Xinxiang. The through train to Hankou was only the first and second express trains. Freight cars were even more difficult, and changing cars mid-way caused even greater losses for merchants. Now, after reorganization, the eleventh and twelfth trains operate between Beiping and Hankou, and the seventy-first and seventy-second trains between Beiping and Shijiazhuang, for a total of seven trains operating in both directions. The twenty-first and twenty-second trains between Beiping and Baoding are also operating on schedule. Currently, in the northern section north of Shunde, there are seventy locomotives, of which thirty-three are damaged. Approximately thirty locomotives are in operation on the line. There are approximately nine hundred passenger and freight cars, of which approximately one hundred and sixty are awaiting repair. Due to years of domestic warfare, the tracks are in disrepair. With the exception of the special express trains, there are often delays in train schedules. Plans are currently underway to restore service.

Goods on the Northern Section: The most revenue on the northern section of the line comes from coal, salt, and general merchandise. The revenue from each special express train is approximately ten thousand yuan, averaging approximately twenty thousand to thirty thousand yuan per day. However, the revenue of the Railway Bureau has peak months and slow months. This winter is expected to be a peak month, but due to insufficient vehicles, it will not be as high as in previous years. The annual revenue of the northern section is approximately ten million yuan. If there were enough locomotives, it could be increased to fifteen million yuan. The revenue of the southern section is mainly from tobacco leaves, grains, and cotton, in addition to imported foreign goods. If the tracks on the entire Pinghan Railway were repaired, the total revenue could be increased to over thirty-six million yuan.

Pay Attention to Floods: In terms of track maintenance, there are sections of the line that have been in disrepair for many years. Temporary light railways are often used to facilitate operations, but they are not strong. If repairs are discussed, a large amount of funding is required. Bridges, in particular, should be given attention. Twenty short bridge tracks are stored in Hankou, and it is proposed to allocate a portion of them to be laid on the northern section. The northern section is mostly derived from the Taihang Mountains, and there is a risk of mountain floods every year. The northern section of the Pinghan Railway has three bridge maintenance sections, whose function is to protect the bridges. The northern bridge maintenance section was originally located on the north bank of the Yellow River and is proposed to be relocated to Zhengding, which is a more central location, making repairs and scheduling more convenient. Furthermore, flood control equipment and personnel are also being prepared. (10th)

Banditry in Xinyu and Tonggu, Jiangxi Province

Xinyu County Seat Captured Twice

Tonggu County Seat in Crisis

Nanchang Correspondence: Xinyu and Tonggu have long been ravaged by bandits. The people of these two counties have repeatedly requested troops for suppression, but there are not enough soldiers to allocate. Now that Minister He (Yingqin) has arrived in Jiangxi, the people of Xinyu in the provincial capital have again requested troops from Minister He. The petition describes the miserable conditions of the bandits' ravages, making it unbearable to read. The document states: "Submitted for the matter of petitioning. Xinyu is bounded by Xingan and Qingjiang to the east, Fenyi and Wanzai to the west, Ji'an, Jishui, and Anfu to the south, and Gao'an and Shanggao to the north. Most of the eastern, southern, and western corners of the county are deep mountains and dense forests. Once the bandits are defeated by our army, they flee into these areas. The people along the south bank of the river have been subjected to their rape, kidnapping, arson, and murder since 1928. The property lost is incalculable. In particular, the two captures of the county seat in 1930 were even more brutal. Apart from Ji'an, no county has suffered more than Xinyu. The county government has sent personnel to conduct on-site investigations. It is estimated that 2,564 civilians were brutally murdered, 5,831 were kidnapped, 37,736 fled, 360 firearms were confiscated, 4,771,100 yuan in property was looted, and 2,761 houses were burned. The fertile fields have been turned into scorched earth, and the people have become vengeful ghosts. The misery is so great that Zheng Xia's "Refugee Map" cannot adequately depict the situation. It is truly an unprecedented catastrophe. We have reported to the provincial government requesting relief and tax exemption, but the government has been unable to provide relief or exemption, resulting in depleted vitality. Now the banditry has returned. On January 28 of this year, more than 3,000 bandits who had been hiding in the southern villages suddenly ravaged the southern areas of the county with over 300 firearms and dozens of horses. Yao Weijun, Wanquan, Sixi, and other places have been occupied. The slaughter and burning are too horrible to bear. The county seat has a garrison battalion that is too busy collecting taxes and levies for the county government to have any spare capacity to suppress the bandits. Fortunately, you, Commander-in-Chief, have arrived in person and will surely be able to plan and win, clear out the bandits, and rescue the people from the depths of misery and lift them onto the cushion of safety. Therefore, we urge you, Commander-in-Chief, to quickly dispatch elite troops to encircle and suppress the evil bandits in Xinyu to alleviate the suffering of the people. The lives of the entire population are in urgent need of rescue."

Page 8

Tonggu is located on the border of Hunan and Jiangxi, and is frequently afflicted by banditry, including arson, murder, looting, and intolerable ravages. Previously, the county seat was captured by Liu's bandits, who looted and robbed extensively, causing incalculable losses. Unexpectedly, at 8:00 AM on January 24, a part of Huang's bandits, who had sneaked in from Paibu, captured the county seat again. The police and militia retreated to Sandu, fifteen li from the city, to gather. The People's Self-Defense Forces of the Fifth, Ninth, and Tenth Districts launched a counterattack in three directions at noon on the 27th, fighting desperately. The two sides engaged in fierce fighting for half a day, with bullets raining down, resulting in numerous bandit casualties and heavy casualties for the police. Later, due to the exhaustion of ammunition, they retreated to their original defenses to hold on and await reinforcements, and urgently telegraphed General Commander Chiang, Chairman Lu, and General Commander He for troops and assistance, expressing their grief and pain. In addition, the bandits in Chong Township of the county, armed for several days, contacted Huang's bandits, and on the 28th, they captured Sandu, Daxia, and Gujiaqiao, massacring thousands of civilians. Corpses were scattered everywhere, and the ground was covered in blood. Some corpses were burned with kerosene and cotton, while others were beheaded and dismembered, with livers and lungs cut out and cooked for consumption. Even Huang Chao and Li Zicheng were not this brutal. The bandits established a Soviet government in the county seat, carried out a "red purge" everywhere, and looted all the goods in the county's shops and the property of the people in the villages, moving them to places like Paibu and Pingtian. They also captured over a thousand men and demanded ransom within a specified period, and raped over seven hundred women day and night. Over three thousand people fled to Xiushui to escape, carrying the old and the young, with cries and wails filling the road. The Tonggu police launched several counterattacks, but they could not succeed due to the exhaustion of ammunition. Therefore, on the 30th, they retreated to Zhengcun in Xiushui to await reinforcements. This kind of catastrophe is truly unprecedented. (February 9)

The Twists and Turns After the Special Tax on Hebei Was Implemented

Tianjin Customs Refuses to Cooperate According to Regulations

The French Concession Forbids the Establishment of Offices

A dispatch from Ping: The special taxes on three commodities in Hebei, namely cotton yarn, cement, and matches, were implemented on the first of this month. Regarding the situation after the implementation, Wu Rongchun, the Chief of the First Section of the Hebei Special Commissioner's Office of Finance and concurrently the head of the Special Consumption Tax Administration, said that since the unified tax was implemented, less than ten days have passed. The goods stored in various firms are currently being inspected and transported, and not many new goods have been declared for taxation. Because the Hebei unified tax is in its initial stage, it is difficult to accurately estimate the amount of revenue. It is estimated that it can generate more than three million yuan per year. Recently, unexpected difficulties have arisen with the Tianjin Customs. Before the implementation of the unified tax, the Hebei Finance Office planned to establish resident offices at Tianjin Customs, Qinhuangdao, and other places to collect the unified tax according to regulations. There were no problems in Qinhuangdao, but unexpected issues arose in Tianjin. The personnel sent by the Finance Office to Tianjin Customs to establish offices and request the Customs to assist in tax collection according to regulations were refused by the Customs Commissioner, who claimed that he had not received instructions from the Shanghai General Customs Office. The Commissioner refused to allow the establishment of offices at the Customs and refused to assist in the inspection and taxation of goods. The personnel of the resident office had no choice but to rent houses near the Customs to set up offices for business. Unexpectedly, as soon as the preparations were completed, the French Concession's Municipal Council used the treaty as an excuse to prohibit the establishment of another tax collection agency within the concession and ordered the office personnel to move to a place near the Tianjin Customs in the Special Third District to temporarily carry out all activities. Currently, Tianjin Customs still refuses to cooperate on the grounds that it has not received orders, only notifying merchants to declare taxes at the office when goods arrive at the Customs, providing only passive assistance. As for inspection and other matters, they cannot be handled according to regulations. Under this circumstance, there are great drawbacks. Foreign goods imported cannot be inspected and taxed at the Customs and can be directly transported to the concession for sale. In this way, domestic goods are subject to the unified tax, while foreign goods can be evaded, which has a great impact on tax revenue and foreign trade. As a temporary remedy, additional personnel have been dispatched to patrol the border between the Chinese area and the concession day and night. Any goods transported from the concession without tax declaration will be immediately detained and severely punished to prevent evasion and provide assistance in case of emergency. Since this problem arose, the Finance Office immediately telegraphed Minister Song to report the situation, requesting him to order the Shanghai General Customs Commissioner to instruct the Tianjin Customs Commissioner to assist in establishing a resident office to implement tax collection, and requesting him to consult with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with the French side, so that the Tianjin French Concession authorities would officially recognize or tacitly approve the establishment of a resident office within the concession. However, no reply has been received since the telegram was sent. Another telegram was sent the day before yesterday (7th), and no reply has been received today (9th). It is now planned to send another telegram to the Ministry of Finance to urge everything, and to send a telegram to Deputy Commander Zhang for instructions. The plan will be determined after receiving a reply.

The Construction of the Shiqi Railway Is About to Begin

The Only East-West Trunk Line in the North

The construction of the Cangshi Railway is of great importance to the transportation and commerce of northern China. During the era of the former Beijing government, the authorities frequently proposed its construction, but it was not realized due to repeated setbacks. Recently, Chinese industrialists Shen Changfu and others, believing that the construction of this railway is essential for the development of Chinese commerce, raised a large sum of money and organized a Shiqi Railway Company, submitting a request to the Ministry of Communications for its construction. It was approved by the Ministry of Communications in August of the 18th year of the Republic. According to their plan, after completing the section from Cangzhou to Shijiazhuang, it will be extended to Qikou Town, which is close to the Bohai Sea. The entire railway is planned to be 290 kilometers long and will be built in four sections. Each section will be opened to traffic upon completion. The first section is from Shijiazhuang to Donglu, 81 li long; the second section is from Shandonglu to Xianxian, 76 li long; the third section is from Xianxian to Cangxian, 67 li long; and the fourth section is from Cangxian to Qikou, 70 li long. There will be a total of 21 stations of various sizes. The important counties and districts it passes through are Zhaocheng, Zhaoxian, Jinxian, Jiucheng, Xinji, Donglu, Shenxian, Wuqiang, Raoyang, Jingxian, and Cangxian, connecting to the Bohai Sea. The area through which it passes is all plains, making it easy to build, and the land is fertile and the agricultural products are abundant, especially peanuts and cotton. After it is built, the export products of southern Hebei and the coal from Shanxi will no longer need to be transported around Tianjin and Qingdao, but can be directly exported from Qikou. According to experts, the terrain of Qikou is very good, and with a little dredging, it can be on par with Tianjin and Qingdao and become an important commercial port in the north. In recent years, those traveling along the Jinpu Railway and wanting to go to the Pinghan Railway, or traveling along the Pinghan Railway and wanting to go to the Jinpu Railway, have felt the pain of detour. In the future, the construction of Shiqi will not only connect the two major trunk lines of the Pinghan and Jinpu Railways in the north and south, but will also combine with the Zhengtai Railway to become the only major trunk line in China. All the fur products of Gansu and Shaanxi will be transported by this railway. It is reported that a capital of 15 million yuan has been raised, and a preparatory office has been temporarily set up in the French Concession of Tianjin. It will be moved to Pingri within the day to officially start work. The procedures for starting construction have also been completed, and construction can begin in mid-February.

The Ministry of Military Affairs Purchases New Weapons

Sends Personnel to Europe, America, and Japan to Purchase

A dispatch from Beijing: The Army Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs, in order to improve the manufacturing of military equipment, has sent personnel to Japan to investigate new weapons for imitation. After these investigators returned to China, they made a list of several items worth studying and submitted it to the Army Department, which then forwarded it to the Minister for review. The Minister approved the immediate purchase of two searchlights with a lens diameter of 1.5 meters. After receiving the approval, the Army Department, in addition to the searchlights, also plans to quickly purchase two work vehicles and attached vehicles for repairing cars, in order to actively study and apply them, thereby enhancing the effectiveness of military transportation. A budget was then prepared and submitted for approval: (1) Each searchlight, including the car, requires 64,000 Japanese yen; (2) a spare reflector requires 3,900 Japanese yen, totaling 131,900 Japanese yen, which is approximately equivalent to 263,800 Chinese dollars; (3) each work vehicle requires 11,000 Japanese yen; (4) each attached vehicle requires 8,800 Japanese yen, totaling 79,200 Chinese dollars. The total cost of all items is 343,100 yuan. This amount has been approved and will be raised by the Military Supply Department, and it has been decided that the work vehicles and attached vehicles will be purchased from Japan, while the other items will be purchased from European and American countries. The Military Supply Department and the Army Department will jointly send staff to make the purchases.

The Qingdao Business Tax Preparatory Committee Is Established

The First Resolution Is to Start with Investigation

A dispatch from Qingdao: The Qingdao Municipal Finance Bureau convened the inaugural meeting of the Business Tax Preparatory Committee at 2:00 PM on the 5th of this month, and also held the first meeting. The representatives who attended the meeting on that day were Zhou Jiayan, Counselor of the Municipal Government; Yin Xuechun of the Public Security Bureau; Dong Zhidao of the Social Affairs Bureau; Lü Tongtang of the General Chamber of Commerce; Guo Binghe, Director of the Finance Bureau; Ruan Xuezhen, Secretary; Xu Sen, Chief of the First Section; Xiong Shubo, Chief of the Second Section; Xiang Zongding, Chief of the Third Section; Yun Ji, Chief of the Fourth Section; Zhuo Jingqian, Director of the Second Section; and Qi Jike. All of the above personnel are members of the Preparatory Committee. At the first meeting, the Finance Bureau proposed to start with investigation first, which was approved for implementation. The Finance Bureau's proposal stated: "Now that the Committee has been established, all preparatory matters should be carried out in order of urgency. It is proposed to start with investigation first, printing investigation forms to be distributed by the Public Security Bureau to each business for self-reporting, and then the Public Security Bureau will order the police to collect them from each household, compile them into册, and submit them to the Committee. Whether this is appropriate is submitted for discussion and resolution." Business Investigation Form: (1) Business Name; (2) Location; (3) Type of Business; (4) Name and Origin of the Business Owner, Manager, or Shopkeeper; (5) Amount of Business Capital; (6) Estimated Amount of Annual Business Income; (7) Monthly Rent of Business Premises; (8) Number of Employees in the Business. Matters to Note: 1. The capital mentioned in item 5 of this form includes all assets used for business purposes, such as public reserve funds and real estate, which are all considered capital; 2. The amount of business income mentioned in item 6 of this form refers to the total income of the business, not the profit; 3. If the business premises mentioned in item 7 of this form are self-owned, please indicate "self-owned" and add the number of rooms; 4. This form must be completed within three days after delivery and collected by the police from each household by the Public Security Bureau; 5. All items listed in this form must be truthfully and in detail reported. If there is any false information, after verification, a corresponding fine will be imposed in accordance with the regulations; 6. Each item of investigation should be additionally annotated below each条; 7. This form is attached with translations in English and Japanese for distribution to foreign-owned stores. (February 6th)

The Future of the Shanxi Arsenal

A dispatch from Taiyuan: After Li Guanglin, the director of the Northeast Arsenal, and Li Yichun, the director of the artillery factory, came to Taiyuan to inspect the Taiyuan Arsenal, Li Yichun returned to Shenyang yesterday to report on the actual situation of the arsenal. Recently, the Shanxi Provincial Party Department and the Post-War Rehabilitation Association have strongly advocated that the arsenal be transformed into a production facility. The Rehabilitation Association also sent Gao Xikong, an employee of the association, to accompany Li to Shenyang to appeal to Zhang Zuoxiang. Regarding the reorganization plan of the arsenal, a certain important employee of the arsenal said, "Since the Northeast sent personnel to inspect the arsenal, we have been ordered to make a total calculation of the machines, workers, and employees of each department of the arsenal. The calculation is about to be completed, but after the calculation, it is not yet clear whether it will be handed over to the Northeast or whether there will be other arrangements. We have not yet received a clear order. Once we have asked for instructions, we can make a concrete announcement. However, we recently received an official letter from the Post-War Rehabilitation Association, which strongly supports the transformation of the arsenal into a production facility. The authorities are said to be adopting this proposal and plan to convert one part of the arsenal into a steel mill, expanding the railway tracks of the Zhengtai Railway to the north to Datong and to the south to Fenglingdu, expanding the transportation of Shanxi as a whole. Another part will be converted into a manufacturing plant for mining machinery, taking advantage of the rich mineral deposits in Shanxi, hiring experts to vigorously exploit them, creating a new path for Shanxi. A third part will be converted into a manufacturing plant for agricultural machinery, hoping to greatly reform agriculture in Shanxi and create modern agricultural lands. Shanxi has always valued agriculture, but in recent years, industry in our country has not been developed, and agricultural implements are all old-fashioned, which has led to the decline of agricultural production. This is a most heartbreaking thing. If Shanxi can take the lead for our country at this time, it would not be bad. In addition, a part will be reserved for the manufacture of military equipment to prevent emergencies. And in fact, national defense cannot but be considered, and it is certainly not a long-term strategy to be without armaments when bandits are rampant."

Anti-Communist Conference in Yanbian

Zhang Shuhan is Ordered to Be Responsible for Handling

A dispatch from Jilin: The Korean Communists in Yanbian are rampant, burning and killing everywhere, and the people are living in misery. The Japanese are also using the pretext of protecting their residents to demand joint police administration. Zhang Shuhan, the Director of the Yanji Municipal Preparatory Office and concurrently the Administrative Supervisor of the four counties of Yanji, Hunchun, Helong, and Wangqing, went to the provincial capital before the New Year and proposed seven plans for governing Yanbian to the authorities. At the same time, various groups in Yanbian also sent representatives to the province to appeal. These representatives and Zhang traveled to Liaoning and Jilin for more than a month. Recently, the authorities finally approved the seven measures proposed by Zhang Shuhan, and Zhang Zuoxiang personally instructed Zhang Shuhan that the local areas of the counties in Yanbian are disturbed by bandits and communists, with frequent cases of murder and arson, which seriously harm the people's livelihood and are of great concern. He was ordered to supervise the county magistrates in properly planning measures for prevention and suppression and reporting to the authorities for review. Zhang Shuhan believed that this trip had yielded results and returned to Yanji on January 17. It is reported that Cui Longzhen, the magistrate of Hunchun County, Xu Hongjian, the magistrate of Wangqing County, and Liu Zuyin, the magistrate of Helong County, arrived in Yanji on the 23rd one after another, and together with Sun Xiangqian, the magistrate of Yanji County, attended the meeting at the Supervisor's Office on the 24th. He also ordered the county magistrates to adhere to the Supervisor's Office and be responsible for prevention and suppression to secure the area and eliminate the Japanese ambitions. It is reported that Yanbian has gradually become more peaceful recently.

Zhang Lisheng's Troops Vigorously Suppress Bandits in Western Chuzhou

A dispatch from Bengbu: After the remnants of Ma Yuren's troops were defeated by Liang Guanying's troops in Jiangsu and fled to the border of Anhui, they were led by the leader Qi Yaozong and joined forces with Jiang Guochang's bandits to occupy the area of Lao Jiashan in northwestern Lai'an. They gathered eight or nine hundred people in that area, with complete firearms and sufficient ammunition. In the past week, they crossed the Jinpu Railway line from Lao Jiashan and harassed the area of Qilin Shangma, Zhulong Bridge, Daliu Dian, and Daishanpu in Chuzhou, and were distributed near Xiaoxi Township, Ma'anshan, Shijiaji, and Dachu, looting and kidnapping, creating a very rampant situation, so that western Chuzhou was disturbed and the people could not live in peace. Xu Peinan, the magistrate of Chuzhou County, telegraphed Zhang Guansheng, the commander of the 2nd Cavalry Division stationed in Bengbu, requesting him to quickly send troops to suppress them. After receiving the telegram, Zhang immediately dispatched Wang Xianzhang's 7th Regiment, Zhang Chuanfu's 8th Regiment, and Ma Jiewu's 12th Regiment, who were stationed in the southern section of the Jinpu Railway to protect the railway, to suppress them. It is now reported that three companies of the 7th Regiment set out from Sanjie and advanced towards Daishan to suppress them, and two companies each of the 8th and 12th Regiments set out from Shaheji in Chuzhou to advance towards Fanshan to suppress them. The bandits first occupied Daishan and Fanshan, relying on the danger to resist, but were then defeated by the fierce combined attacks of the troops and fled to the southwest. They reoccupied four or five villages, trying to resist stubbornly. The bandits occupying Dazhang Zhuang were broken by the companies in the snow, and many bandits were killed, many hostages were captured, and several bandit flags were captured. Only three soldiers were injured. The bandits were greatly frustrated in this battle, and the remnants of Ma Yuren's troops suffered even greater losses. It is said that only a hundred people remained, and they fled to Zhulong Bridge with Jiang Guochang's bandits. The troops of the 2nd Cavalry Division are still tracking and pursuing them. During this winter defense period, when businesses are settling their accounts, they rely entirely on telephones for quick communication. Zhenjiang Business Association Decides to Extend Small Railway Station Loan: The Zhenjiang Business Association recently received a letter from the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Bureau regarding the extension of the branch line from the small railway station to the Zhenjiang customs station, requesting the immediate preparation of funds for construction. Since this project requires more than 134,000 yuan, a meeting must be held to resolve the issue. Therefore, a meeting of executive committee members was convened yesterday afternoon at 3:00 to discuss the method. The following resolutions were made: (1) Reply to the Railway Bureau agreeing to the railway extension plan to the customs station; (2) Regarding the earthwork and land work, etc., totaling 32,900 yuan, it will be undertaken by the association. The purchase of land and various construction materials totaling 101,470 yuan will be funded by the Railway Bureau, and the association will provide a loan; (3) A total of 134,370 yuan will be borrowed from the banking industry by Chairman Lu, with each industry responsible. The following methods were also discussed: (1) The association will lend 100,000 yuan to the Railway Bureau, to be repaid monthly from the Railway Bureau's business income, with 10,000 yuan to be repaid monthly without interest for ten months; (2) The principal and interest of the 32,900 yuan undertaken by the association and the interest on the 100,000 yuan loan will be added to the wharf tax of 20 cents per ton for railway freight in the port, with a term of two years. After clearing the principal and interest, the remainder will be used to dredge shallow waters near the station and wharf; (3) The Railway Bureau must start construction as soon as the tide recedes. The Railway Bureau is responsible for any overruns in the budget or losses in the project. All of the above must be contracted by the association and the Railway Bureau and handled in accordance with the agreement.

Security Office Executes Huaian Police Captain for Aiding Bandits: The Jiangsu Provincial Security Office previously received a police captain named Cao Zhixiang from Huaian County, who was accused of colluding with bandits and harming the people. After a detailed interrogation, he admitted to colluding with bandits and was sentenced to death. The sentence was reported to the provincial government for review and approval, and yesterday (12th) at around 10:00 AM, he was taken to the North Gate execution ground and executed by firing squad. In addition, two bandits from Danyang, Ni Songshan and Yao Yunqing, were also sentenced to death and were sent to Danyang yesterday by clerk Zhang Bingyan for execution.

Yangzhou

Administrative Sanctions in the County Middle School Case Are Final: Bao Han, the principal of Jiangdu County Middle School, was accused by Shi Songyu and others of embezzling public funds. The case was ordered by the provincial government to be thoroughly investigated, but the files were stolen and transferred to the judiciary. The investigation court held four sessions, but no prosecution has been filed. However, it is heard that the administrative aspect has now been transferred by the provincial government to the Department of Education for separate sanctions. The general meaning of the document is that the director of the bureau, Chen Da, was negligent in preventing the theft of the bureau's files and failed to solve the case in a timely manner, which is a dereliction of duty and should be recorded as a major demerit, and he should be given a deadline to investigate the person who stole the files and hand them over to the court for punishment in accordance with the law. As for Principal Bao Han, although there is no evidence of theft, he is indeed suspected of embezzlement and should be dismissed from his position and await judicial resolution. The position of principal should be filled by the county magistrate, who should promptly select and submit candidates for review and appointment. It is now heard that County Magistrate Chen has selected three people and submitted them to the Department of Education for selection.

Gaoyou

Education Sector Demands Salaries: The education sector in the county has been in arrears with salaries for five months. With the end of the year approaching for shops, the teachers and staff are in urgent need of money. Yesterday (10th) at 3:00 PM, the directors of various social education institutions and the principals of various schools went to the county government to meet with County Magistrate Wang and request that he order the Finance Bureau to quickly raise more than 70,000 yuan to fully pay the outstanding salaries. The meeting ended at 8:00 PM without any results. This afternoon at 3:00 PM, the directors of various social education institutions and the principals of various schools will go to the county government again to discuss the matter with County Magistrate Wang.

Pinghu

Two Bandits Killed North of Xincang: On the afternoon of the 10th, two bandit ships with more than 20 bandits were discovered near the Dacheng Nunnery north of Xincang Town, Pinghu. A Jiangsu provincial army happened to pass by and saw the bandit ships. They ordered a search, but the bandits landed and ambushed themselves by the river and opened fire. More than 20 quilts and several bags of clothing were found on board.

Reporting Embezzlement of Fines for Punishment: He Wenyao, the fifth squad leader of the ninth Pinghu Water Police Team, embezzled fines. Chamber of Commerce Cables Request for Delay in Levying Business Tax: The Jiaxing County Chamber of Commerce Unification Committee stated that the business tax will soon be levied, but the various tax rates set are several times or dozens of times higher than the regulations promulgated by the Ministry. Merchants and people in various places believe that the burden is too heavy to accept and have submitted petitions to the authorities for separate reductions. Therefore, yesterday, they cabled the Department of Finance, ordering the various bureau chiefs to postpone the levy until the draft is approved by the Central Government, the tax rates are determined, and the merchants and people can accept them, in order to avoid disturbances.

Reconciliation in the Lian Sidang Demolition Case: In Jiaxing's Lian Sidang, Yan Jintai and others organized the Taishan Fishing Company and built a curtain to raise fish in the pond. It is now learned that a third party came forward to mediate, persuading Yan and others to abandon their losses. Yan has accepted an unconditional resolution, so the case can be temporarily concluded.

Continued Interrogation of Pirates Who Ambushed Xinning-Taiwan Vessels: The Overseas Water Police Bureau dispatched the Jinghai warship and other vessels to encircle and suppress the pirates who robbed the Xinning-Taiwan vessels. It is now learned that those who went to encircle and suppress included the Third Guerilla Squad, the Sixth Water Patrol Squad, and the Seventh Water Patrol Squad of the Water Police Bureau. As a result of the encirclement and suppression, the pirates Ying Gongshan, Liang Meichuan, Chen Xianwei, Jiang Shaomei, Li San, Li Xin’s wife, Li Xiangmao, Li Xiuyun, Lu Yuanbo, Huang Haicai, and Zhang Dewu and others, totaling twelve people, were captured alive. Six Russian rifles, four local quick rifles, two German rifles, one nine-shot pistol, one mainland rifle, and one six-inch hand cannon, totaling fifteen firearms, were seized. When the soldiers and bandits were engaged in fierce fighting, the bandits were unable to withstand the pressure and attempted to escape by large boats, but the bandit boats were sunk by artillery fire from the Jinghai warship, killing twenty bandits. After the guerilla squad and water patrol squad directly attacked the bandit’s lair, they also killed more than fifty bandits and rescued twelve hostages. On the water police side, Water Police Xiang died in battle, and Chen Renjie and Jin Gao were injured. The water patrol squad and others fought fiercely with the bandits for a long time, consuming a total of 4,446 bullets and two shells. The water patrol squad and others have jointly reported the encirclement and suppression to the Water Police Bureau, which has forwarded it to the Department of Civil Affairs for review.

Bandits Everywhere in Fenghua (1): A nun named Jing’an, who lived in Baiyun Nunnery, located about one mile outside the South Gate of Fenghua, had some savings. One night a few days ago, six or seven bandits suddenly came and looted at will. All valuables were taken away. (2) Bandit chiefs Sun Libiao, Shen Yong, etc., led their followers and anchored four boats in the Shitou Ya Sheng Ke area of Fenghua, making them temporary bandit lairs. For days, they sent letters to wealthy households in nearby villages, extorting huge sums of money. It is heard that Wu Gongfan, a wealthy household in Daqi, received a letter demanding 20,000 yuan, and Wang Shuqin received a letter demanding 10,000 yuan. Zhou Heting of Chunhu Street also received a letter demanding 2,000 yuan, all of which were to be raised within three days. (3) At around 3:00 PM the other day in Zhanghu Village, Songlin District, Fenghua, more than 50 bandits arrived with the intention of kidnapping wealthy people. More than 30 brave young men in the village resisted with guns, which angered the bandits. The bandits then shot people on sight, killing more than 30 people.

Hangzhou

400,000 Stones of Rice in the Urban Area: In the past, Hangzhou's rice supply mostly relied on external sources. However, due to the abundant harvests of crops last year, supplies were readily available, and prices gradually decreased. In December of last year, the city's rice prices slightly increased, with top-quality rice increasing from eleven yuan to twelve yuan and two dimes. Recently, there have been more sources of supply, and sales have been sluggish. The recent rice reserves total more than 400,000 stones, which can supply the urban area for two to three months.

Inland Water Launches Announce Suspension of Service: The inland water launches in Zhejiang Province, due to the Lunar New Year holidays, which cannot be avoided, have been decided by the various bureaus to suspend service uniformly from yesterday (13th). As for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company launches, which are managed by the Department of Construction, they will continue to operate as usual in accordance with the new calendar. The resumption date for the various launch bureaus has not yet been determined.

Putting it Aside with a Smile, Hai Ke

Husband (asking his wife): Aren't you satisfied to have married a husband like me? Wife: Yes. I'm not quite satisfied. Husband: What shortcomings do I have? You might as well tell me.

Wife: You don't quite measure up to my ideal husband.

Husband: What should your ideal husband be like? Wife: I want him to be strong and heroic, yet silent and peaceful, so that I can look up to him and admire him.

Husband: Then you might as well go to London, England, and marry the statue of the naval hero Nelson.

Teacher (to the students): Today, I want to talk to you about the way of love. You should love each other.

Student: How should we love each other?

Teacher: You should love each other as brothers. And my position is that of your father.

Student: Father, I want a dollar to buy chocolate candy.

Car Salesman: Sir, this car is both beautiful and sturdy. You definitely won't regret buying it.

Young Man: Let me try it first. My fiancée can drive too. I have to let her try it. I think the steering gear and brake system are not properly installed. She will definitely feel uncomfortable when driving.

Car Salesman: Our car is imported. How could it not be properly installed? I think you should get another fiancée.

Miscellaneous Affairs of Wu Peifu

He Lin

A guest came from Sichuan, recounting Wu Peifu's trivial matters, quite humorous, so I recorded them one by one. It was previously mistakenly reported that Ziyu, the scholar, was critically ill. Now it is known to be inaccurate. The reason for the misreport is also seen below.

Yang Sen Calls Wu His Poetry Disciple: Wu was in Sichuan, taking shelter under Yang Sen. Yang Sen was somewhat versed in literature and has enjoyed writing poetry since the year before last. He occasionally sent his poems to Wu. Wu would revise them and send them back, with a few words of praise. Thus, Yang Sen wrote to Wu, often calling himself Wu’s poetry disciple. Wu also liked to tell people about it, saying that if Yang Sen abandoned military affairs and devoted himself to poetry, he would become his indoor disciple.

Calligraphy and Paintings Widely Circulated in Sichuan: Wu would respond to those who asked for calligraphy and paintings, instructing his doormen not to hinder them. He used to only paint bamboo, but recently he also became capable of painting orchids. The inscriptions on the paintings were all his own poems. When writing for others, he initially wrote in cursive script, but now he also writes in official script. He was very busy keeping up with the demand.

Hiring People to Carve More Than a Hundred Seals: There was a man from Sichuan named Jin Yunhe who was skilled at stone carving. Wu praised him highly at first sight, saying that this man's iron pen captured the legacy of Deng Shiru. He invited him to meet and asked him to engrave seals. It is said that in one or two years, he carved more than a hundred seals for Wu. In addition to engraving ancient poems and his own poems, most of them were titles Wu had given himself after entering Sichuan, such as "Failed Hero," "Sour Scholar," "Old Sour," "Drunk Lying on the Battlefield," "Literary Soldier," "Retired Veteran," and "Gardening Hermit." There were countless others like these, mostly containing feelings of injustice. When painting orchids, he often used Banqiao's phrase, "Breaking the Black Basin to Enter the Mountain," a seven-character seal. Observers said that it fit his position exactly.

Recently Called Himself the Four No's Elder: Wu was ill in the autumn and bedridden for more than half a month. He once composed several dirges and elegiac couplets on the spot. Outsiders mistakenly reported that he was critically ill, probably due to this. The narrator only remembered his elegiac couplets, saying, "When successful, be honest and conscientious, do not take concubines, and do not accumulate money. Drinking and composing poetry is still the nature of a scholar. After failure, be stubbornly determined, do not go abroad, and do not go to the concessions. Gardening is a genuine return to the countryside after retiring from military service." The gatekeeper said that both the upper and lower couplets used the word "not," which seemed repetitive. Wu laughed and said, "This is not the examination hall of the former Qing Dynasty. What does repetition matter?" Therefore, he called himself the "Four No's Elder." It is also said that the dirges contained phrases such as "millions of sand worms and three thousand iron cavalry." He was skilled in antithesis, and his energy was strong, so it is known that he will not die soon.

Recording the Madness of Rabid Dogs

Qing

A few days ago, rabid dogs were discovered biting people in our county (Jiading) city. It was around 8:00 AM, when there were many pedestrians in the city center. Therefore, those who were bitten could not avoid it. Thus, the disaster caused by rabid dogs was even more severe than in the past. This time, it finally gained the attention of the local authorities. This must be recorded, and it is also hoped that it can be remedied in the future to avoid this undeserved disaster and to avoid suffering this poison again.

The rabid dog on that day came from the Dry Grass Bay outside the East Gate, only five or six miles from the city. It was raised by a certain family. The dog's body was not very large and was yellow and white. It was actually an ordinary pet dog. It is not known why it suddenly acted like a family dog going mad. It ran straight to the vicinity of the East Gate, passed through Spring Bridge, went southeast to Xie Jing, turned back and entered the city. It first arrived at Qiliang School next to the City Temple, almost harming it. The school used the telephone to call the County Public Security Bureau, urging them to take precautions. The dog had already reached the west side of the East City Bridge and had bitten several people. The most seriously injured was a villager who was selling straw sandals. Both of his knees were bleeding profusely and dripping to the ground, so he had to leave in pain. The police officers on the roadside at the time did not take it seriously and ignored it. Unexpectedly, the dog passed west of Zhou Bridge and turned south again, passing through Ordinary School. It bit a female student surnamed Li who was about to enter the school. Fortunately, she was not injured because she happened to use a book in her hand to defend herself, so only the book was destroyed by it. The strangest thing was that a woman surnamed Yan, who lived with her husband's family outside the West Gate, happened to come out of her house that morning and encountered the dog. Because no one was catching the dog, it was allowed to run wildly out of the city, and the woman happened to meet it, so she was bitten by it. She tried to resist with her hands, but her palms and the tiger's mouth were invaded by its claws and teeth. Her poisoning was probably the same as the villager's, or even worse. It is estimated that the dog bit more than 30 people that morning. Their names could not be determined in detail. Later, it was finally beaten to death with a stick by someone in Xilu Village, west of the Huiji Sauce Garden, and sent to the Cunren Hospital in front of the pagoda in the city to test for the presence of rabies.

Zhang Hongnian's family in Qiannanli, our county, raised a small dog that looked like a lion and was so playful that people loved it. It was said to have been obtained from a man surnamed Gao in Shanghai. In the eleventh month of last year, his sister-in-law was bitten by it. Before long, she died. Those in the family who were fortunate enough to avoid the poison had to spend a lot of money on medical treatment and medicine. There was a suggestion to ban dog ownership, but the authorities turned a deaf ear. This time, at the initiative of Gu Xuchu, the district chief of the first district of the city, all dog owners must use muzzles, otherwise the Public Security Bureau will be responsible for catching them. He also purchased various kinds of rabies medicines from Shanghai and ordered the city police to investigate those who had been bitten and quickly come to the hospital for injections. He also warned the public with cans to guard against unforeseen circumstances. This is indeed an urgent matter that the local authorities should not delay. Therefore, I am happy to record it.

Things to Know About Raising Dogs

Qiu Shui

Western women love dogs, and it has almost become a fashion. Since the eastward spread of European customs, it is often seen on the streets that Chinese men and women take dogs with them. It is generally known that dogs have gained the universal love of mankind. Because there are so many Westerners who love dogs, the art of raising dogs has become a specialized discipline. In addition to the cat and dog barbershops in New York and London, there are also specialized cat and dog hospitals. Various magazines often publish various kinds of common sense about raising dogs. I have selected the essentials and translated them to share with enthusiasts.

(1) Every morning, drive it out of the house to let it get some fresh air and to allow it to excrete as much waste as possible. Over time, it will become a habit, and the room will not be soiled, which will hinder hygiene.

(2) Dogs should be washed regularly to remove dirt and prevent disease. However, after washing, it must be wiped dry with a dry towel and then combed with a comb, otherwise it is easy to catch a cold or suffer from lung disease.

(3) Winter is a dangerous time for all kinds of animals. Dogs are no exception. Dog owners should clothe them during the day and provide them with a warm dog bed at night. The bed should always be kept clean and frequently brushed to avoid the growth of pests.

(4) If a dog's body is unclean, it is easy to breed lice. Washing it from a young age with medicated soap or puppy soap (available in pharmacies) can prevent this.

(5) If a dog's blood is unclean, it is easy to cause mange. At this time, in addition to washing frequently with medicated water, it is also advisable to seek medical attention quickly, otherwise the mange will spread to the human body, causing no small harm.

(6) Dog food should be refined, not much. Beef is the only good product, but it should not be eaten too much, and it should not be mixed with salty juice.

(7) Dogs should not eat salty food or ham bones, otherwise they will have an unpleasant odor.

(8) Dog necks should not be constantly tied with straps.

(9) Dogs must be treated with both severity and kindness.

(10) A dog's nose is usually wet. If it is dry, it must be sick. It should be treated quickly.

(11) During the mating period of female dogs, they should be mated with males of the same species, otherwise it is easy to cause difficult labor.

(12) Long-haired dogs should have their hair cut in the summer so that the dog's body is cool. After autumn, the hair will grow longer and shinier.

Travel Notes from Southeast Asia

(119) Ling Hua

What is noteworthy is the life habits and thoughts of the lower classes of India. These are black people, also known as Kala people. After all, Chinese people have a habit of self-importance and look down on all kinds of people, calling them mixed names, such as calling Westerners "red-haired devils," Burmese "old Burmese," and black people "black devils." Black people have the most pitiful lives and are the largest laboring class in various parts of Southeast Asia. I was very sympathetic to their lives in Singapore and briefly recorded them. I remember once I lived in the New Mountain Temple and was about to enter, but the door would not open. I was carrying things and could not open the door myself. A Kala person passed by and respectfully opened the door for me. I was very happy. When I got to Burma, there were even more black people, and the Burmese were quite polite, serving very carefully. When they met people, they would pull rickshaws and give them money, which they would receive with both hands and express their respect. If they walked in front of people, they would bend over and bow. (Burmese women also do this.) Chinese people also treat them badly. For example, if they give them rickshaw fare and they argue, they will hit them with a stick, and they will run away. And Burmese women often order them to pull rickshaws without giving them money. These people often sleep in the gaps between people at night and spend a dozen or so copper coins a day. However, they are not only laborers. Their nature is extremely docile and without complaint. I am very strange about this. Compared to the current labor community in China, whose momentum is increasing a thousand miles a day, with the momentum to overthrow capital and the intellectual class, and the tea room in the Guangdong Inn is especially strange because it does not accept calls and does not entertain guests. When I asked people who knew the situation in India, I learned that the reason why the Kala workers in India are so poor but do not complain is due to the Indian religion. Indian religion says that when humans were first born, the first class of people was divided from a certain god's body. They were born from the god's head, so they are the most noble and are monks. The next class of people was born from the arms, which is also noble, so they are emperors. The next class of people was born from under the belly, so they are merchants. The lowest class of people was born from the lower part, so they are laborers. This Indian class system was created by mythology. This religion has not declined to this day, so laborers are not resentful and are willing to come from the lowliest of families. The Buddhist scriptures often say that the Chandalas walk on the road without daring to stand in front of people, fearing that people will touch them, so they shake their tin staff to avoid noble people. Monks should also be humble when they leave home and learn to "shake the tin." The source of the two words "shake the tin" is also. To this day, the Kala workers are so content with their lives and do not regret it. I am very surprised at the depth and difficulty of changing the divine religion, and that the Buddha's equality has failed to change it in thousands of years. Moreover, Buddhism has completely failed. From this point of view, politics is indispensable. Things will turn around when they reach the extreme. The large number of Kala people in India, if they encounter the teachings and movement of Russian workers in the future, will be transformed from inferiority to sacredness. I am afraid that there will be a day when they will hold their heads high in the world and should not be underestimated.

Warmth in the Heart

(370) Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 17: Emerald Eyebrows with Skills to Preserve Youth, Golden Market for Horse Bones, No Way to Extend Life

That foreigner... after fitting the wristwatch on Hua Yuanchun, he scrutinized it again. He held her hand, patted her shoulder, and then chattered with that guest for a while. Hua Lao Liu softly said to the guest, "That foreign gentleman who receives the misfortunes... he's praising me, isn't he?" The guest said, "He's complimenting you. Why would you scold him? He said your arm is very white, and wearing that wristwatch makes it look even whiter. If it were on a thin wrist, it wouldn't look so good. Because your hand is so white and smooth, it looks especially fitting." Whether it's Chinese or foreign, men or women, they always take to flattery and sweet words. Hua Lao Liu was happy to hear that the foreigner also praised her, of course she was willing. She also greeted the foreigner with a smiling face. The guest said, "Then it's this one." Hua Yuanchun nodded and said she didn't know how much it cost. The guest said, "Don't worry about it. I'm giving it to you." He chattered with the foreigner again. The foreigner took out a small booklet from his side, used a fountain pen clipped to the pocket of his Western-style vest, signed a slip, and gave it to the foreigner. The foreigner bowed to them both, then put the wristwatch in a purple leather case, inside a box lined with blue satin. He handed it to Hua Lao Liu. Hua Lao Liu didn't know how much the wristwatch cost. She couldn't read foreign words, nor did she know how much the guest's signed slip was for. It wasn't until the two of them were sitting in the carriage that Hua Yuanchun asked the guest how much it cost. The guest said, "A small matter, four hundred and fifty dollars. It was originally going to be five hundred, but because I recognized that foreigner a little, I had done business with him before, so he gave me a 10% discount." Hua Yuanchun was naturally very happy. At that time, wristwatches were just becoming popular among women, and hers was a white gold wristwatch with embedded diamonds. When she went to performances or the theater, it glittered in the many lights. Many unsophisticated young sisters saw it and asked, "Sixth Elder Sister, how did you buy a silver wristwatch?" Hua Yuanchun smiled proudly and said, "This wristwatch is called platinum." One young sister said, "Oh, is platinum more expensive than gold?" Hua Lao Liu said, "I heard it's twenty times more expensive." When people asked her how much she bought it for, she added some exaggeration, randomly saying seven hundred or eight hundred dollars. People half-believed it. Later, that guest returned to Nanyang. Hua Lao Liu, to commemorate that guest, still wore it on her hand. One day, somehow, a small diamond around the wristwatch fell off. It was that little A'bao, who, although small, had very sharp eyes. She saw a shiny thing in front of the bed and asked, "Is this from your ring?" Hua Yuanchun looked. There were no missing stones on the ring. Looking again at the wristwatch, there was a small gap left.

Commercial News

Gold and Money Markets Show Soaring Prices Again

High of Nineteen Taels

Fluctuations Reach Thirty-Three Taels. Yesterday, February 13th, the price of gold saw a sudden and sharp rise of twenty taels. However, market changes are unpredictable, with fluctuations of several to ten taels constantly. The situation in the Persian Gulf is turbulent. Throughout the day, there was a discrepancy of thirty-two to thirty-three taels, which is a significant amount. It seems that both official and unofficial foreign exchange rates are strained. Listed prices have been reduced by two and a half points. As for trading on the floor, it remains stable and active. In the early market, Hongli, Yuanxing, Yongcheng, and Fengyong all made purchases. Zhifeng, Yongxin, Hengyuan, and Maoyong all occupied the selling side. Overseas silver markets have reported lower prices, with the U.S. markets closed for a holiday. However, the initial gold price was flat. Subsequently, because there seemed to be more sellers, it once retreated near the fifty tael mark. Afterwards, buyers were eager, and prices rose again. There was a slight pause, but at noon, the exchange rate became more expensive. Furthermore, major players such as Hengxing, Taikang, Runyuan, and Xingyong showed strong buying interest, especially with frequent and sharp price increases. The price suddenly jumped out of the seventy tael mark, rising sharply by two taels. Later in the market, Taikang, Run, Hongli and other companies continued to buy, while Hengxing had already sold. Foreign exchange became even tighter. Moreover, there were rumors that overseas telegrams reported a sharp drop in silver prices, making it difficult to remedy the situation. Upon hearing this news, the market sentiment suddenly surged, and prices rose by more than ten taels, quickly exceeding the 780 tael mark. In an instant, a storm arose. Hengxing and others sold, and also learned that the Indian exchange rate fell and then rose, causing a sharp drop of more than ten taels. The situation seemed foolish and aimless, drifting with the wind. Finally, the total was fifty-four or five taels. Yesterday afternoon, the industry had already made forward swaps privately. The multi-party initially posted six or seven taels, then five taels eight or nine cents, and then raised it again to seven taels. The Dalian and Guangdong groups, including Hengxing, had mutual swaps. It is said that Hengxing first swapped in short positions, about three thousand contracts. Also, many firms completed transactions. This morning, large contracts may continue to fall slightly.

Morning Trade Soars Straight Up. The gold market for March opened this morning with a slight increase of five cents, totaling 756 taels and five cents. Although large bars of silver are down by sixteen and five-tenths of a cent, silver prices are uneventful, and the European market is uncertain, so the market sentiment is also flat. Subsequently, due to sales by companies such as Tongtaichang, Zhifeng, Yongfuchang, prices fell sharply from 57 and a half taels to 49 and a half taels. Suddenly, HSBC and others bought May British gold at 123.75, and then the price rose again by more than four taels, totaling 54 taels. The initial price was announced as two and a half taels, and the listing was reduced by 125 US dollars. The 25th gold was up one and a half points. Chengfengyong and Hengxing and others bought in, immediately increasing the price to 55 taels. Then, Xinhang sold it, and it retreated again to 52 taels. After 10 o'clock, Hengxing bought again, and Taikangrun, Yuanheng, Yuanxingyong and others came to buy, especially with British gold being mutually transacted by banks from 1225 to 16875. Therefore, the gold price rose by 7 or 8 taels until 11:00, totaling 60 taels. Then it immediately depreciated by more than one tael. Yuanchengyong, Hongli and others bought in again, reaching 62 taels at 11:30. Zhifengyong Xinhang sold out. In just seven or eight minutes, it dropped by two taels. Suddenly, Yuanxingyong, Yuanhengtangkangrun had released it, showing a charming appearance. The total reached 67 taels and five cents. By the time of the noon closing at 66 taels and two cents, the British gold suddenly changed and was reduced by 125 US dollars. The 5th gold was increased by one and a half points, and the buyers were excited. The price continued to be made to 72 taels. The initial listed price was 823 taels and four cents, reduced by eighty taels or so. At noon, it was changed to 840 taels and 06 cents, reduced by sixty-eight or ninety taels.

Local News

The Anti-Opium Society Firmly Opposes Opium Public Sales

Eight Proposals Passed

Determined to Oppose to the End

The Chinese National Anti-Opium Society, due to various rumors that the anti-smoking authorities are changing their policy of complete prohibition and adopting a plan for public sales of opium, and because the newly appointed anti-smoking commissioner Wu Liande has publicly advocated for public sales, and Li Jihong has gone to Taiwan to study public sales methods for emulation, believes that the matter is of extreme importance to the future of opium prohibition. Therefore, a temporary executive committee meeting was held yesterday morning at Mr. Tang Shaoyi's residence on Bazhi Road. Attendees included Honorary Chairman Tang Shaoyi, Chairman Wang Jingqi, Vice Chairman Li Denghui, legal advisor Cai Rudong, executive committee members Mrs. Bing Guoyou, Shen Gao, and Ding Shu, representatives from the Zhejiang branch, general manager Chen Lingyun, general manager of the society Huang Jiaohui, and secretary Chen Hongjun. Chairman Tang Shaoyi announced the purpose of the meeting, stating that the promotion of public opium sales has moved from theory to practical possibility, which he considers a very serious situation. He believes that the society should unite with various public organizations to oppose it, gather the opinions of the majority, and submit a petition to the government, requesting the strict implementation of opium prohibition and the establishment of more drug rehabilitation hospitals, ordering current opium addicts to quit within a specified time limit. The discussion of the proposals then began, resulting in the following resolutions: 1. To hold a joint meeting of Shanghai public organizations to oppose public opium sales on the afternoon of the 19th of this month at 3:30 PM, to arouse public attention. 2. To petition the central government to strictly prohibit opium and, based on Sun Yat-sen's anti-drug instructions, declare that opium will never be used as a source of revenue, and to immediately abolish the special opium tax in the two Hu provinces. 3. To petition the Legislative Yuan to immediately enact laws prohibiting the public sale of opium. 4. To petition the Central Party Headquarters to publicize and prevent public sales based on Sun Yat-sen's anti-drug instructions. 5. To send letters to Commissioners Zhong Ke and Ma Yinchu, urging them to strongly oppose public opium sales to the authorities. 6. To send a letter of advice to the Central Anti-Opium Committee. 7. The case of whether executive committee members of this society should be allowed to concurrently serve as members of the Central Anti-Opium Committee will be submitted to the general assembly for a vote. 8. To issue a declaration opposing public opium sales and state that Wu Liande's proposal for public sales is his personal action and completely contradicts the overall position of this society. All of the above proposals were passed and handed over to the secretariat for active implementation, in order to emphasize opium prohibition and benefit anti-drug efforts.

Severe Penalties for Absentees from Sun Yat-sen Memorial Week

The City Executive Committee Formulates Five Measures

The Executive Committee of the Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters holds a Sun Yat-sen Memorial Week every Monday morning at 9:00 AM. In addition to reporting on the work of the past week, committee members rotate weekly to lecture on Sun Yat-sen's teachings, and a staff member is selected by lottery to present a prepared speech on Sun Yat-sen's teachings. This practice has been very successful. Recently, five disciplinary measures for absenteeism have been stipulated as follows: (1) Any person absent three times within two months will be dismissed from their position. (2) Two requests for leave within one month will be counted as one absence. (3) Staff members requesting extended leave must state their reasons, and the training department will submit the request to the executive committee for a decision. (4) Staff members on official duty will not be considered as having requested leave or being absent. (5) Staff members selected to speak who fail to do so will be considered absent. It is reported that the above measures were approved at the 87th executive committee meeting the day before yesterday and have been communicated to all departments for the information of their respective staff members.

German Ambassador to Return Home on Schedule

Departing from Shanghai on the 17th aboard the Jingguo Maru

German Ambassador Borch has been recalled to his country. He traveled south by train from Beijing to bid farewell to Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting and important figures of the National Government. He arrived in Shanghai the night before last and was hosted by the German Consul and the German community in Shanghai at a farewell banquet yesterday afternoon. He is scheduled to return to Germany at 8:00 AM on the 17th aboard the Jingguo Maru of the Japanese Mail Steamship Company. Foreign Minister Wang has instructed Liu Yunfang of the Foreign Affairs Office to represent him at the Waibaidu Bridge Wharf to see him off and provide all necessary assistance.

Newly Appointed Director of Telegraph Bureau, Rong Baoyi, Took Office Yesterday

Former Director of the Telegraph Bureau, Mr. Chen Xizeng, has been reassigned as Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. His vacancy was filled by Rong Baoyi, appointed by the Ministry of Communications. Rong, accompanied by former Director Chen Xizeng, went to the bureau together by car yesterday morning to take over. Chen introduced the old staff of the bureau, and Rong gave a speech, stating that in the past, due to the loss of sovereignty, military and political affairs were largely controlled by foreigners. Now, the Ministry of Communications is actively working to recover these rights. The development of telegraph administration and the responsibilities of telegraph personnel will increase day by day. He humbly stated that he was ordered to take over, but felt that his knowledge and experience were inadequate, and hoped that all colleagues would work together. Chen then proceeded with the handover formalities. It is said that he officially took office today, without any ceremony. There will be no inauguration ceremony. The internal personnel of the bureau will remain unchanged.
