Mr. Chen Jitang, Commander-in-Chief of the Eighth Route Army, arrived in Shanghai the morning before yesterday. Yesterday afternoon, Shanghai Mayor Zhang Yuejun hosted a special banquet for Mr. Chen and his wife at the Dahua Hotel, as well as Lin Yizhong of the Guangdong Provincial Committee. Mr. Chen's wife has never been to Hangzhou, so they have decided to take the Shanghai-Hangzhou express train to Hangzhou this morning (the 14th) to visit. Those traveling with Mr. and Mrs. Chen include Lin Yizhong and Lin Xiangding. They will stay in Hangzhou for four or five days before returning to Shanghai and then to Guangdong.

Chu Minyi Discusses the Twenty Academic Expedition

Detailed Account of the Sino-French Itinerary

Developing Resources Begins in the Northwest

Yesterday, newspapers in Beijing reported on the news of a "French Kangzang Expedition," which does not entirely correspond to the facts. Knowing that Chinese Committee Member Chu Minyi was the leader of the Chinese side of the expedition, a reporter from the Guowen News Agency visited his residence to inquire about the truth. Mr. Chu gave a very detailed reply, which is recorded below. Chu said that previously, Sino-French academic organizations formed an organization called the Nineteen Academic Expedition, which was based on sixteen articles of cooperation between Mr. Li Shizeng, representing the Chinese Academic Organizations Association, and the Citroen Automobile Company and Mr. Yu An, representing the French government. Each side appointed a leader. The Chinese side was led by himself, and the French side was led by a man named Haardt. The articles of cooperation stated that each side would appoint a number of members to form the expedition. French members must be reviewed and appointed by the academic organizations association of their country. The route was as follows: the French side would use seven Citroen-Kégresse vehicles, departing from Europe, passing through Asia Minor, Turkishistan, and arriving in Yining, Xinjiang. The Chinese side would also use Citroen-Kégresse vehicles shipped from France, departing from Tianjin, passing through Beijing, Zhangjiakou, Suiyuan, Ningxia, Lanzhou, and arriving in Dihua. Then they would meet with the French members. Because the borders of Xinjiang have many high mountains and steep ridges, Citroen-Kégresse vehicles are not easy to pass through, so the French had to abandon their vehicles and walk across the border of Xinjiang, then switch to vehicles departing from Tianjin and return to Beijing, then turn around and travel along the Hankou Road to Hankou, then along the Yuehan Road to Longzhou, and then to Annam. At this point, the Chinese side of the expedition came to an end. The French side would continue to advance, from Annam to India, and back to Europe. The time spent in China was only five months, just passing through, and there was no time to collect antiquities. The Chinese side took this opportunity to use Citroen-Kégresse vehicles to inspect the northwest, which would surely yield results. It can be predicted that the development of resources in the northwest in the future will begin with this expedition. He recalled that he had inspected the Suiyuan and Zhangjiakou areas the year before last and knew that China's resources were in the northwest. If the northwest is not developed, China will remain poor and weak for a long time. If efforts are made to develop it, it will surely become rich and strong. Therefore, he said that the future of Chinese industry today is like that of the United States in the past, and it should start with efforts to develop the west. The reason why the expedition did not take place last year was that both sides were not prepared, and he had to go to Belgium to participate in the World's Fair. The expedition has now been renamed the Twenty Academic Expedition. Both sides are prepared and the departure date should not be far off.

Chinese Cotton Production Improvement Statistics Conference

Jointly Initiated by the National Cotton Industry

Conference to Be Held for One Week Starting March 15th

Since 1919, the Chinese Cotton Mill Owners Association has been engaged in domestic cotton production surveys, spanning a decade. Limited by financial resources, progress has been slow. Currently, this survey has been generously supported by provincial cotton fields and major cotton industry organizations in various cotton-producing provinces, who have provided personnel to assist. In terms of survey personnel, it has reached perfection. Considering that improvements are needed in terms of economics and organization, and that surveys in previous years have been too late and of little use, it is urgent to change to estimation methods to meet needs. Initially, it was planned to invite cotton fields from various provinces currently engaged in cotton production surveys to hold a cotton production statistics conference to discuss estimation methods suitable for the whole country. Later, the attendees were all provincial cotton fields, and the majority opinion was to take this opportunity to add the issue of cotton production improvement to the discussion. Therefore, the scope of the meeting was slightly expanded and renamed the Chinese Cotton Production Improvement Statistics Conference. Currently, Jiang Dixian of the Chinese Cotton Mill Owners Association, Yang Xiandong of the Hubei Cotton Crop Improvement Committee, and Wu Weijing of the Zhejiang Provincial Cotton Industry Improvement Field are responsible for the preparations. The details of the conference are as follows: (A) Initiators: Jiangsu Provincial Cotton Industry Improvement Committee, Shandong Provincial Cotton Industry Experimental Station, Henan University Agricultural Extension Department, Shaanxi Provincial Agricultural Cotton Experimental Field, Shanxi Provincial Agricultural Cotton Experimental Field, Hebei Industrial Department Zhengding Cotton Industry Experimental Field, Hunan Provincial Cotton Industry Experimental Station, Anhui Provincial Agricultural Experiment Station, and this association. The initiators are the provincial agricultural fields, cotton fields, or cotton industry organizations currently engaged in cotton production statistics. Other cotton planting and cotton industry organizations will be invited to attend for guidance. (B) Objectives: (1) To connect the provincial cotton fields, agricultural fields, cotton planting organizations, and domestic cotton planting industry engaged in cotton planting in various provinces, and to jointly discuss the overall improvement strategy of national cotton production. (2) To determine the cotton production statistics and estimation methods applicable to the whole country. (C) Conference period: The opening ceremony will be held at 2:00 PM on March 15th and the closing ceremony will be held on the afternoon of March 21st, a total of one week, with one meeting in the morning and afternoon each day. (D) Reports and speeches: Representatives from various provinces will report on (1) the current situation of cotton crops, (2) past improvements, and (3) future plans. Domestic cotton industry experts will be invited to give speeches, with topics divided into four categories: (1) breeding, (2) promotion, (3) statistics and estimation, and (4) others (trade, fiber engineering, etc.). It is planned to invite twelve lecturers to give one speech in the morning and afternoon each day. (E) Proposals: In addition to proposals from the initiators, proposals on "improvement" or "statistics" from the domestic cotton industry are extremely welcome. Please send them to the meeting early. (F) Address: Chinese Cotton Mill Owners Association, 86 Edward Road, Shanghai.

Reasons for Silk Mill Shutdowns

Financial Difficulties, Cocoon Shortages, Taking a Short Break

After the New Year, silk mills in this city borrowed money from the financial community to start work due to a slight increase in silk sales in Europe and America. However, this was just a flash in the pan, and European and American silk sales declined again, with silk prices plummeting by more than 100 taels. Although prices have risen by 20 to 30 taels due to exchange rate fluctuations, the shortage of cocoons and high prices have made it difficult to cover costs. It is difficult to sell at a loss. In addition, the accounting period of the silver and money markets has arrived, and the repayment of silk cocoon mortgages is very urgent. The government's assistance to the silk industry and the issuance of public bonds will take time. Unable to sustain operations, most of the more than 40 silk mills that had started work took advantage of the annual closure and announced shutdowns yesterday.

Managers of Various Bookstores Spoke at the Municipal Propaganda Department the Other Day

Handling of Reactionary Publications

Report from the Municipal Propaganda Department

The Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters Propaganda Department has always paid close attention to cultural institutions in this city. Recently, it planned to separately convene representatives of various cultural institutions to discuss and negotiate everything. On the afternoon of the 12th (the day before yesterday) at 3:00 PM, managers of bookstores in this city were convened for a discussion. Representatives from the New Life, New Universe, Qingyun, Yonghu, Qunzhong, Huatong, World, United, Modern, Taidong, Guanghua, Yadong, Kaiming, Commercial Press, Beixin, Zhonghua, New Moon, Dadong, Dajiang, Guangming, Literary, Qun, and Nanqiang bookstores, totaling more than 30 people, attended. Cai Hongtian, Zhou Hanmei, Li Zheng, Cai Bubai, and others from the Municipal Propaganda Department attended. Cai Hongtian, Secretary of the Propaganda Department, chaired the meeting, and Chen Ming recorded the minutes. At the beginning of the meeting, after the ceremonial greetings, the chairman reported, stating that Shanghai is the center of the publishing industry in China, and the representatives of the more than 30 bookstores present today are the focus. Therefore, the significance of today's discussion is very important. If the publishing industry in Shanghai can embark on an accurate path, it will not only guarantee the peace of mind of the ideological circles and society in this city, but also clarify the ideology of the whole country. Since 1915, the ideological circles in China have seemed to have a vigorous new atmosphere, but who knows that this has been exploited by the most reactionary factions, leading to bizarre and extremely chaotic situations. Therefore, the Party has had to ban reactionary publications. It should be known that this kind of ban is not done willingly. However, a small number of people in society are unaware of this and believe that freedom of speech and publication is enshrined in the Party's program, so the current ban is self-contradictory. It should be known that freedom is not without restrictions. If freedom is excessive, it is a crime. Otherwise, adultery, robbery, and arson would be freedom. This kind of freedom will surely lead to national destruction. This is not just the case in China. Governments around the world prohibit the publication of dangerous books, or revise them. Within Soviet Russia, the existence of even one book of the Three Principles of the People is absolutely prohibited. Therefore, banning reactionary publications is not reprehensible and cannot be reprehended. However, most bookstores in this city are commercial in nature. Publishing reactionary publications is not due to a political background or political activities, but is the result of competing for novelty and being manipulated by reactionary female thieves in the literary world. Therefore, the Municipal Propaganda Department is deeply concerned about the losses of bookstores on the road to prohibition, and that is why today's discussion is being held to negotiate with each other to make up for the losses. Today, two issues that are hoped to be discussed are: (1) Banned books should be burned immediately. (2) In the future, it is best to submit books for review to this department in advance to avoid unexpected losses after printing. Next, Zhou Hanmei of the Guidance Section and Li Zheng of the Editorial Section gave reports successively. Then, representatives of various bookstores expressed their opinions and jointly discussed the methods, scope, and standards of reviewing manuscripts. It is reported that satisfactory results were achieved.

Question of Establishing a Maritime Administration Bureau

Shipping Companies Have Not Expressed Support or Opposition

The Ministry of Communications believes that China's maritime administrative power is controlled by the Marine Department of the Customs, which seriously affects China's sovereign right to communications. It has proposed to the National Government to define the scope of powers and establish maritime administration bureaus in Shanghai and other places to manage all maritime affairs. The State Council has formally approved this. This city is also one of the places where a bureau will be established. A reporter from the Guowen News Agency inquired with shipping companies yesterday and recorded the situation as follows: Organization of the Maritime Administration Bureau: This matter has been noisy for a long time, for more than two years. It is intended to establish a general bureau in Shanghai, with the following branches: (1) Nanjing (also in charge of Pukou), (2) Zhenjiang (also in charge of Tongyang and Huaiyun), (3) Suzhou (also in charge of Suxi), (4) Haizhou, (5) Hangzhou (also in charge of Jiahu and Zhejiang), (6) Ningbo (also in charge of Zhenhai and Zhoushan), (7) Wenzhou (also in charge of Oujiang and Taijiang), etc. Yang Ying (Zixiong), the current acting principal of the Wusong Merchant Marine School, was appointed as the director of the Shanghai bureau. The bureau was located on the fourth floor of 6 Huangpu Beach. However, due to various procedures, it could not be formally established. On February 3rd of this year, the State Council discussed it again, and the result was to revise the established places to (1) Shanghai (also in charge of Jiang, Zhejiang, and Anhui ports), (2) Hankou (also in charge of Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Sichuan ports), (3) Weihaiwei (also in charge of Zhili, Shandong, Liaoning, and coastal ports), (4) Harbin (also in charge of Songjiang and Heilongjiang ports), (5) Hong Kong (also in charge of Fujian, Guangdong, and Guangxi provinces). The Ministry has followed the order of the Executive Yuan to implement it.

The Shipping Association's View: Shipping companies generally welcome the government's intention to use this to recover maritime rights. Former Director Yang Zixiong, believing that the government has re-proposed the matter, is eager to establish the Maritime Administration Bureau. A few days ago, he specially visited the leader of the shipping industry, Yu Qiaqing, to ask for his support. Yu replied that the matter concerned the entire shipping industry and would be submitted for discussion at the meeting. At the general meeting of the Shipping Association the previous week, no decision was made on this issue, and neither support nor opposition was expressed. After hearing this news, Director Yang went to Nanjing to ask the government for instructions. He is expected to return to Shanghai in the next few days. According to reliable sources yesterday, the Executive Yuan believes that although the establishment of the Maritime Administration Bureau has been decided by the government, the consent of the Shanghai shipping companies must be obtained beforehand before it can be formally organized. As such, the matter has been noisy for a long time, and the date of its establishment is still far away.

Joint Business Effort to Study Business Tax

Various Trade Associations Present Opinions

Two Research Associations Seek Mutual Verification

The Guomin News reports that since the National Government officially ordered the abolition of the Likin tax and implemented the collection of business tax, businesspeople across the country have paid close attention to it. The business community in this city is even more enthusiastic, with various trade associations organizing tax rule research committees and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce establishing business tax research committees. Although seemingly self-organized, their research targets are the same. The two associations plan to exchange and verify their research results to gather a wide range of opinions and achieve consensus. The following are excerpts of telegrams from various parties: (1) The various trade tax rule research committees to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce business tax committee: Respected Sirs, It is our considered opinion that imperfect national systems are directly sufficient to stifle production development and indirectly sufficient to hinder national prosperity. Therefore, tax rules in democratic countries must be passed by people's representative bodies to ensure that they align with the principle of people's livelihood. Our country, however, has just celebrated unification, and the period of political tutelage is just beginning, with formal representative bodies of the people yet to be legally established. The government authorities have declared that they are extremely willing to listen to public opinion when formulating new taxes. Therefore, the various trade associations, recognizing the importance of tax rules, and to embody the sincerity of the wise authorities, in order to thoroughly complete tariff autonomy and promote the implementation of new taxes, have dispatched personnel to organize our association, whose duty is to study the perfection of the tax system and assist the government authorities where they fall short. Your organization has led the city's business community and your past suggestions on tax matters have always been insightful. This time, you have paid particular attention to the business tax in this city, organizing a specialized committee to conduct research. Moreover, the committee members are all outstanding individuals and respected figures in the business community, who will undoubtedly benefit the party, the country, and the business community in the future. Our associations are intrinsically linked, with common interests and should work together. We are sending this letter to inform you that if you have any opinions in the future, please notify this association in time so that we can exchange research and consult with the authorities for adoption, so that the opinions of the business community can be expressed in a unified manner, etc. Your profound insights are deeply appreciated. We hope that you will forward this to the members of the business tax research committee of your association, so that they may promote progress and explore verification at any time. Then, the national tax system will truly rely on progress, and not only will the various industries benefit. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce. (1) The Luodian Chamber of Commerce of Baoshan County to the Tax Rule Research Organization (details omitted): We hereby request that you relay the opinions of the merchants as follows: (1) All businesses operating within the territory should be taxed uniformly. Merchants' businesses vary in size and are based on goods. Some goods are manufactured, some are wholesaled, and some are retailed. Now, the tax rate is set such that manufacturing has a manufacturing tax, wholesaling has a wholesaling tax, and retailing has a retailing tax. Most of the goods in rural stores are purchased in bulk. If they are taxed as business tax, it is actually a third layer of taxation. (2) If business tax is already collected by the central government, should special taxes, such as tobacco and alcohol taxes, be collected as before? In rural towns, shops that sell oil also sell alcohol, and shops that sell paper also sell tobacco. The daily income cannot be divided into separate accounts for oil, alcohol, paper, and tobacco, to be cleared one by one. How should taxes be handled at the time of payment? (3) Taxes are paid monthly, and tax collectors can check their account books. Those with false accounts will be fined. Merchants' account books cannot be separated from the store for a day. If officials pick faults and harass them, there is no shortage of excuses to impose guilt. They will take away the account books and force them to pay fines, leading to endless troubles, even worse than the old likin system. The above points have all been reported by the stores in the city. Although they may be overly cautious, the matter is indeed inevitable. We should request your association to consider how to further address the government. If you can turn it into public opinion, we would be grateful (details omitted). (1) The Egg Industry Association of this city to the Tax Rule Research Organization: It is our understanding that eggs are a secondary product of farmers and a necessity for consumption, and should not be regarded as a luxury business. Moreover, the egg business has the greatest risks, the most losses, and the lowest profits. It is frequently subjected to foreign suppression, and most businesses already find it difficult to support themselves. If they are subjected to heavy taxes, regardless of their short lifespan, since the government takes business as the standard, without regard to profit or loss, uniform taxation will occur. At this time of egg industry decline, after the abolition of likin, with the industry barely recovering, how can it withstand heavy taxation again? We should request that a telegram be sent to the Executive Yuan, imploring it to consider the great importance of the egg industry to the national economy and the people's livelihood, and approve the lowest possible tax rate. Furthermore, the egg industry in this city mostly purchases goods from the interior, only buying and not selling. We have heard that egg farms in the interior will also be required to register and pay taxes. When shipping out, those with customs will report export tax, and those without customs will remit and pay import tax. In the future, when resold overseas, export tax will also be required. After the business tax is levied in the three cities, taxes will also have to be paid. This is one item taxed four times. We do not know if this conflicts with the regulations. If it does, we especially request your association to represent the heavy taxation, as egg merchants cannot afford it. Please approve the lowest possible tax rate for the egg business. Also, the business tax issue in Shanghai should still proceed according to the steps decided at the second representative conference. When it is necessary to hold it, all Chinese and foreign stores should be treated equally to show fairness. In addition, this city has not suffered losses from the abolition of likin, and it seems that it should follow the provisions of Article 4 of the regulations, requesting a rate that should not exceed two per thousand and should be appropriately reduced to ease the burden on the business community (details omitted). (1) The New Medicine Industry Association of this city to the Tax Rule Research Organization: We have read the regulations for the collection of business tax in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, and the tax rate for Western medicine is as high as 20 per thousand, and 15 per thousand. We are shocked. Medicine is for treating diseases and is of great importance to people's lives. It is by no means comparable to luxury goods. The tax rate set by Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces for medicinal materials is 2 per thousand. Why is there such discrimination for the same medicine? If we do not strive for it, we fear that the Shanghai Municipal Government will also want to use this as a ratio when formulating the business tax to be collected in the future. Our association will not recognize it. We are sending this letter to request your association to uphold justice and quickly send a telegram to the People's Government and the Executive Yuan to instruct the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces to correct it in order to alleviate the difficulties of the business community and maintain the lives of the people (details omitted).

Tea Association Requests Reduction of Business Tax

A Document Submitted to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Yesterday, the Shanghai Nanshi Tea Trade Association convened an executive committee to study the business tax. Mr. Yang Shangting chaired the meeting, stating that if the business tax rate is collected at 5 per thousand, the industry will not be able to withstand it. It was decided to submit a request to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward it to the financial authorities, requesting that it not exceed 2 per thousand in accordance with the regulations. The document submitted to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday stated that it was a request for a reduction in the business tax rate in order to maintain national production and benefit the business community. Our association has received reports from member companies stating that the business tax for tea shops in Shanghai is to be levied at 5 per thousand. In recent years, sales of Chinese tea have greatly decreased, and the tea industry has reached its limit. If this large amount of business tax is levied again, it will directly put domestic production in a desperate situation. The tea production volume is mainly from Anhui, Zhejiang, Hunan, Fujian, Jiangxi and other provinces. Taking Zhejiang Province as an example, when rural farmers pick tea leaves in the spring and summer, they sell them to the nearby temporary tea shops, which must be subject to a business tax once. Then, the tea shops in the rural towns sell them to the large tea shops in the provincial capitals or urban areas, which must be subject to business tax again. Then, they are resold to the tea shops in Shanghai, which must also be taxed. When the Shanghai tea shops resell them to tea shops, they must also be taxed. The goods from the place of origin to the tea shops are already taxed four times. However, the abolition of Likin and the increase in taxes is a good intention to consolidate and alleviate the difficulties of the business community. Now, there is a proposal to collect 5 per thousand, which violates the regulations. It is stipulated in Article 4 of the provinces taxation regulations that where luxury goods and items with a need to be banned are concerned, this would not be the case. It can be seen that the government's intention is to prevent taxation from being unrestricted everywhere, which would harm businesses instead of benefiting them. This is why there are such strict regulations. Even Dr. Ma Yinchu, a member of the Legislative Yuan, stated during a speech at the Municipal Party Headquarters on the business tax rate, "The business tax levied on capital should not exceed 10 per thousand, and the business tax levied on business should not exceed 2 per thousand." His statement was also based on the regulations. Now, because our members cannot afford this large amount of business tax, they unanimously request that your association forward this to the Ministry of Finance and the Shanghai Municipal Government to handle it in accordance with the regulations. Please do not exceed 2 per thousand for the business tax of our industry in order to maintain national production and benefit the people's livelihood.

Repercussions from the Tianjin Bureau's Excessive Tax Collection

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Industry Association received a telegram from the Tianjin Meida Cigarette Company, stating that Luo Chengwei, Director of the Hebei Cigarette Unified Tax Bureau, together with Song Manshan, who purchased them, and Liu Yusheng, the investigation director, colluded to engage in corruption and arbitrarily overcharged. This invisibly increases the cost of Chinese cigarettes by eight or nine yuan, and the value of foreign goods is already balanced. Their harm to national goods and violation of laws and discipline are unprecedented. Store Employees' Salaries Calculated Monthly According to the National Calendar

No Need to Provide Supplementary Compensation Due to Discrepancies from the Lunar Calendar

Since the National Government officially ordered the implementation of the National Calendar, the Shanghai Pharmaceutical Industry Association, because of the difference in the number of days in the National Calendar year and the Lunar Calendar year, the general pharmaceutical workers took this opportunity to request that the employers make up for the wage difference, so they sent representatives such as Sun Meitang to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, requesting instructions on whether to compensate for the wage difference. Yesterday, we received a response from the bureau, which stated: "We have received your request. The payment of wages to employees in the industry has always been calculated on a monthly basis. Now that the National Calendar is being implemented, it is appropriate to calculate it according to the months of the National Calendar. Please inform them accordingly. This concludes the response.

Rental Housing in the City Center

The Municipal Bureau of Public Works Seeks Design Plans

Since the Shanghai Municipal Government delineated the city center area, it has spared no effort in planning and management. All matters concerning the road system and zoning plans in the area have been announced successively, as reported in previous newspapers. We have recently heard that the Municipal Bureau of Public Works, considering the city center area to be a rare piece of land in the city, requires all buildings to strive for perfection. Now that the new municipal government building has been scheduled for the groundbreaking ceremony on July 7th of this year, the rental housing in the commercial and residential areas will inevitably be built in time. If there are no standard drawings for reference, it will be difficult to design and arrange them properly. With the approval of the municipal government, it has decided to first solicit standard design plans for reference by investors and builders. The first prize winner can receive a prize of 1,000 yuan, and the second and third place winners will receive different prizes. We have found the origin and solicitation methods and are eager to disclose them as follows:

Origins of the Solicitation: In recent years, land prices in this city have been increasing, and construction materials and labor costs have been rising. Investors and builders of rental housing often focus on short-term interests and pay no attention to the safety and comfort of tenants. Therefore, most of the houses built are simple and outdated, not meeting the needs of the times. The building regulations can only correct the overall structure of the upper course. As for whether the width and depth of the house are appropriate, whether the interior layout is suitable, and whether the exterior of the building is as good as it should be, we still have to seek active improvements in addition to passive restrictions. In view of this, the bureau held a solicitation for standard design plans for rental housing in the city in 1928. At that time, domestic architectural experts enthusiastically responded, and the bureau evaluated and published a special book. The progress of the construction of rental housing in the city in the past two years has been greatly assisted by the guidance of these standard design plans. Now that the urban center area has been determined, and the road system and zoning plans in the area have been announced successively, the construction of housing in the commercial and residential areas as needed will be carried out one after another. However, the city center area is observed by the entire city, and no matter what kind of building, if it is not carefully designed and arranged by architectural experts, it will not be a model. Therefore, we are holding a second solicitation for prize money, with April 15, 1931, as the deadline. We hope that domestic architectural experts will be enthusiastic about municipal administration, express their talents, and not be stingy with their pearls.

Solicitation Methods: (1) Scope of Solicitation: A section of urban housing in the commercial area of the city center area and its entire layout, a section of housing in the residential area of the city center area and its entire layout. Applicants should apply for both types of designs. (2) Design Standards: Applicants should pay close attention to the current social and economic situation in this city in order to ensure that these designs can be used as a standard for construction. (A) Style: The exterior of the house should be generous and beautiful, and should preserve the oriental style. However, the old-fashioned shikumen often gives residents a sense of depression and must be avoided. (B) Cost and Land Price: The cost and land price of each building should not exceed 40,000 yuan (assuming the land price in the residential area is 3,000 yuan per mu), and the cost of each urban house should not exceed 50,000 yuan (assuming the land price in the commercial area is 6,000 yuan per mu). (C) Building Area: The building area in the residential area should not exceed 40% of the total area, and the commercial area should not exceed 60%. (3) Interior Layout: The urban house should be divided into bedrooms, dining rooms, kitchens, and toilets, in addition to the storefront. Each residence should be designed for one family, with at least one bedroom, one living room, one dining room, one kitchen, one servant's room, one storage room, one toilet, one bathroom, and one clothes drying area. Assuming that there are no complete ditches around this section, attention should be paid to the equipment for accommodating sewage near the city houses or residences. (4) Designs: (A) The required designs are as follows: (1) The entire site plan of the houses in each section (scale 1/150). (2) The entire bird's-eye view of the houses in each section (colored). (3) The front view of each house (scale 1/50). (4) The floor plan and roof plan of each floor (scale 1/50). (5) The section view of each type of house (scale 1/50). (6) The entire cost estimate and description. (B) The position of all equipment and daily necessities in the room should be clearly drawn. (C) The drawing paper must be high-quality white thick drawing paper, 60 cm wide and 90 cm long. (D) Except for the bird's-eye view, all drawings must be drawn with black ink and must not be colored. (E) All texts in the drawings, except for numbers, should be written in Chinese, and the dimensions should be in metric units. (5) Prizes: The first prize is 1,000 gold yuan, the second prize is 500 yuan, and the third prize is 200 yuan. If only one of the two designs is selected, half of the prize money will be awarded. (6) Notice: The solicitation methods and maps can be obtained from the Fourth Section of the Bureau of Public Works, Maojia Lane, Nanshi, Shanghai. Applicants who have any questions about the solicitation methods can send an anonymous letter to the bureau for inquiry. The bureau will immediately copy the original letter, together with the reply, and send it to each applicant. However, if there are any letters after March 21, 1931, they will not be answered. (7) Secret Marks: Do not write your name on the design drawings, just make a secret mark in the lower right corner of the drawing paper, and write your name, experience, place of work, and the secret mark used on the design drawings on another piece of paper, seal it in an opaque envelope, and submit it with the drawings. This letter will be opened by the judges after the designs have been evaluated. (8) Evaluation: The evaluation of the designs will be handled by a committee organized by experts. After the evaluation, the winners will be notified by the bureau and announced in major newspapers in this city. (9) Sending Designs: The designs must be properly sealed and sent by registered mail or delivered to the Fourth Section of the Bureau of Public Works, Maojia Lane, Nanshi, Shanghai, for a receipt. (10) Deadline: April 15, 1931, is the deadline and will not be extended. (11) Ownership of Designs: The winning designs will not be returned, and the bureau may reprint special books and publicly exhibit them for reference by citizens.

Merchant Inland River Vessels Also Suspend Service

No Goods or Passengers on Any Routes

Forced to Stop Sailing

Since Shi Zhaoji took over the Merchants' Inland River Steamship Bureau, he has implemented austerity policies. The Zhejiang Construction Department has remitted more than 10,000 yuan in cash to support the reorganization of various routes. The small inland river steamers in Shanghai have been suspended since the 11th. The bureau is a government-run agency, and Shi Zhaoji decided to operate as usual. However, since the 12th, the steamers on the Suzhou and Hangzhou routes have been departing with no goods to load and no passengers traveling, and he would be wasting fuel, which would not benefit the bureau. Considering the economic situation, he telegraphed Hangzhou to request permission to suspend service. The reply was received yesterday, and the bureau's steamers on the Suzhou, Hangzhou, and Huzhou routes will also be suspended and will not depart until the 23rd.

Measures for Transporting Rice to Zhejiang

The Beijing-Shanghai and Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Traffic Departments require that rice transported to Zhejiang must be inspected by the Rice Inspection Office before it can be released. Now that the agency has been abolished, special temporary measures for transporting rice have been established. Yesterday, all station masters were instructed to follow them. One of the measures is listed below: (1) For foreign rice declared in Shanghai, the customs declaration form should be checked before it can be loaded. (2) If the rice is in transit from Jiangsu Province to Zhejiang Province, the passport should be checked. (3) If there is no customs declaration form or passport, the forwarding station master should ask the cargo owner or the forwarding company to issue a temporary bond, stating that the cargo owner is responsible for any accidents or detentions by the state agency.

Red Cross Northeast Special Envoy Departs

Li Zhenbang to Depart North Tomorrow

The Chinese Red Cross Society has learned that various places in the three northeastern provinces have been using the name of the Red Cross to take actions outside of established procedures. The vast distances make inspections difficult, and it is difficult to distinguish between good and bad, which has a great impact. As a result, the work of the various branches is also difficult to progress. Therefore, honorary public relations officer Li Zhenbang has been appointed as the Northeast inspector to guide the branches to work hard and reorganize everything in order to achieve unified national development. He is scheduled to depart by ship tomorrow.

Joint Conference of National Medical Associations

Discusses the Registration of Doctors in the French Concession

Yesterday, the Shanghai Medical Association convened various medical associations at Yizhixiang to discuss all important issues. Representatives from the National Medical Association, Xu Naili and Wang Wanbai, representatives from the Chinese Medical Association, Niu Huisheng, Chu Minyi, Le Wenzhao, and Zhu Hengbi, representatives from the Pharmaceutical Association of the Republic of China, Xia Dongchu, Zhu Qiluo, and Liu Buqing, representatives from the Shanghai Medical Association, Song Guobin and Ye Zhisheng, secretary Zhu Shansong, representatives from the Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Medical Association, Fang Jiacheng, Cao Fangtao, Wang Shushu, and Ni Liansheng, and representatives from the Shanghai Branch of the Pharmaceutical Association of the Republic of China, Cai Yumen, and others, more than a dozen people were present. Song Guobin was elected as the chairman. First, Chu Minyi and Niu Huisheng reported on the process of contacting the Bureau of Health regarding the registration issue in the French Concession. The result was very satisfactory. Three methods were discussed on the spot, requesting the Bureau of Health to adopt public opinion and strive for the right: (1) The organizational law of the Ministry of Health has not yet been promulgated, and the registration in the French Concession cannot be delayed. Therefore, it is proposed that all members of formal medical organizations who have proof can obtain a temporary certificate from the Bureau to open a clinic in the French Concession and register directly. (2) According to the French Concession's regulations for the registration of doctors, doctors residing outside the French Concession who want to see patients in the Concession must first obtain a license. Because these methods are close to harshness, it should be requested that the Bureau protest that physicians whose professions have been approved by the National Government do not need to obtain a license in each concession. (3) The French Concession's regulations for the registration of doctors state that a fee of 2 yuan must be charged annually for obtaining a license. The means is complicated and should be handled according to the regulations of the National Government and to levy a permanent payment one time. The above three articles were unanimously approved and the matter was proposed by Wang Wanbai. Then, the examination regulations for Western medicine physicians published by the Examination Yuan were discussed, and it was decided that opposition to the examination methods in the regulations should be expressed. The matter was handed over to the medical associations to convene meetings separately, discuss in detail, and then decide. Song also discussed other cases and adjourned.

Total Number of Death Sentences in the Public Concession Last Year

Total of Forty-Four People

The Da Mei Evening News reports that a total of 44 criminals in the Public Concession were sentenced to death by the court last year. Of these, 42 were sent to the Junhe River in Jing for execution by shooting in accordance with the Law on Punishing Bandits, and the remaining two were convicted of murder and sentenced to hanging in accordance with the criminal law. But that is a significant decrease compared to the previous year, when a total of 77 criminals were sentenced to death in 1929, including one woman who was sentenced to hanging for conspiring with her lover to kill her husband.

Telegram Regarding the Disastrous Military Calamity in Zheng County

Telegram Received by the Red Cross from the Henan Relief Association

The Chinese Red Cross Society received a telegram from the Henan Relief Association, which reads: "To the esteemed Chinese Red Cross Society, according to a report from Xie Zechao, the Magistrate of Zheng County, since April, rebel troops have been entrenched in the county, dispatching over 4,000 soldiers in total. Airstrikes have destroyed over 280 houses, and there have been losses of over 2,300 large and small carts, and over 32,100 livestock. Over 1.34 million catties of rice straw and over 53,000 stones of rice were requisitioned, along with donations and requisition fees totaling over 710,000 yuan. Losses from wartime labor, damaged crops, and plundered clothing are valued at over 360,000 yuan, bringing the total estimated losses to over 4.16 million yuan in silver. These figures are verifiable. Other losses are not included. Currently, the affected people lack food and clothing, and are suffering amid the cold weather at the end of the year. We earnestly request your immediate transfer to relief efforts." It is noted that Zheng County is the center of the Pinghan Railway and a strategic location where the rebel forces congregate. The situation is dire and support is urgently needed. The rebel troops have directly seized everything possible, leaving the populace with no means of livelihood. After the looting, the remaining people are left waiting for death. We earnestly hope for swift relief efforts. [Signed] Zhang Fang, Henan Relief Association.

Local News II

Grain Merchant He Jiechun Kidnapped

Dragged from Rickshaw and Taken Away in a Car

The Rickshaw Puller Exhausted and Unable to Give Chase

He Jiechun, a grain merchant employed at Tongxingtai Firm at the intersection of Sichuan Road and Fuzhou Road, residing at 231 1/2 Xixinglong Lane, Chongqing Road, was abducted at approximately 11 PM the night before last. He was riding home from work in his private rickshaw when, upon reaching the lane entrance, he was suddenly kidnapped by four men. Yesterday morning, the victim's family reported the incident to the Xinzha Police Station, requesting an investigation. As of yet, there are no leads. He Jiechun is a local, 45 years old, who has been in the grain business, also dealing in exports. He uses a rickshaw for his daily commute. On Thursday night, he visited a friend at the Far East Hotel regarding business matters, not returning home until after 11 PM. As the rickshaw approached the entrance of Xixinglong Lane, two men suddenly approached in the rain, behaving suspiciously. The first man walked to the front of the rickshaw and, without asking any questions, grabbed the rickshaw puller, Ah Er, by the chest, loudly asking the person behind him, "Is this him?" The man replied yes. At this point, He Jiechun, bewildered, peered out of the rickshaw canopy to see what was happening. To his surprise, the two men in front had already started tearing the canopy apart. They took a step forward and, with four hands, pulled He Jiechun out, exclaiming "Get in the car!" They led him to a car with guns and forced him inside. The car immediately started and headed south. The rickshaw puller, Ah Er, initially filled with righteous indignation, took off in pursuit. The kidnappers' car turned south and then east, entering the British Concession via Manila Road and then the French Concession via Danshui Road, eventually disappearing on Route des Soeurs. By this point, Ah Er was exhausted and out of breath, left with nothing to do but return in despair, report to the victim's wife, and then report to the police station. According to the rickshaw puller, the car's license plate appeared to be a black plate number 403, but after investigation, the police suspect that this is a forgery.

Four Corpses Dug Out of the Fire Site on Baotong Road

A Mother Firmly Embraced Her Son, Their Bodies Completely Charred

Two Apprentices Unable to Escape, Losing Their Lives

The fire at the Gui Xiang Cun cigarette paper and sundry goods store at 452 Baotong Road, Zhabei, at 11:30 PM the night before last, which consumed five buildings, was reported in yesterday's paper. When the fire broke out, firefighters were busy extinguishing the blaze and could not immediately determine if there had been any loss of life. It was only known that several people were missing. It wasn't until 2 AM yesterday morning, when the fire was completely extinguished and it was light, that workers were hired to sift through the ashes and found four bodies, including the store owner's wife, Fan Zhu Shi, her son, Fan Yuanshou, and apprentices Gao A Chun and You Mou. The store owner, Fan Jingchu, had jumped from a window to escape after the fire broke out, suffering injuries to his legs and arms, and has been hospitalized. The total loss of goods and property is estimated to be no less than seven or eight thousand taels of gold.

Four Lives Lost: The Gui Xiang Cun cigarette paper and sundry goods store was opened by Fan Chu, a Ningbo native, who had leased the land to build the store eight or nine years ago. The business was doing well. Its location was at the intersection of Baotong Road and Zhonghua Xin Road, and it was bordered by a fence on the Zhonghua Xin Road side, beyond which was a cemetery, preventing access. Therefore, the main entrance was next to the Zhou family mansion. On the night of the fire, the Fan couple and the store employees were all asleep. The store owner's wife and son lived upstairs, while the two apprentices lived downstairs. After the fire broke out, Fan's wife, Zhu Shi, immediately took her son and tried to escape down the stairs, but the door was locked and could not be opened immediately. By the time she tried to go back upstairs, the staircase had already been burned through, leaving them trapped. The two apprentices, Gao and You, also died at the same time. When Fan Zhu Shi's body was found yesterday, she was still firmly embracing her son, Yuanshou. Both bodies were completely charred, a truly tragic sight. The deceased, Fan Zhu Shi, was 42 years old, her son Yuanshou was 12 years old, and the two apprentices were Gao, 16 years old, and You, 18 years old.

Adding Fuel to the Flames: The five buildings at number 452 were interconnected. Although firefighters tried their best to put out the fire, the flames were too fierce and beyond control. In particular, dozens of boxes of kerosene stored in the Gui Xiang Cun were also affected, adding fuel to the flames and making the situation even worse. There are various theories about the cause of the fire. According to reports received by the police, the fire started downstairs. The Gui Xiang Cun sundry goods store had stocked up a lot of goods due to the upcoming Lunar New Year, and everything was reduced to ashes in the fire. The losses were significant. The insurance coverage was only for two thousand taels.

Two Kidnappers in the Cai Fulin Case Sentenced to Death

The Other Three Accomplices Given Life Sentences

The Police Station Will Appeal the Acquittal

Cai Fulin, a comprador for the British American Tobacco Company, was first kidnapped on March 14 of the 18th year of the Republic [1929], and was released after a ransom of 30,000 yuan was paid. He was kidnapped again last year and released again after another ransom of 30,000 yuan. This past winter, the kidnappers in both cases were successively apprehended by Chief Detective Lu Liankui and others, and were handed over to the Special District Local Court for investigation. It is now known that Zhang Jinsheng, a colleague of Cai Fulin, masterminded the first kidnapping, with nine accomplices in total. After questioning, Judge Ge Zhitan announced yesterday afternoon that Zhang Jinsheng and Qiang Hong were each sentenced to death for the crime of jointly kidnapping and demanding a ransom. Jin Cangshou, Wang Daoshi, and Chen Wu Shi were each sentenced to life imprisonment. The four ransom letters were confiscated. Zhang Qian Shi, Chen Xianglong, and Shao Renmei were found not guilty. Wang Yaotang, the lawyer for the police station, argued that Zhang Qian Shi, as Zhang Jinsheng's wife, and Chen Xianglong, also a colleague of Cai Fulin, were both accomplices and should not have been acquitted. The police station found this verdict unacceptable and immediately announced that they would appeal the acquittal of these two individuals. Judge Ge then ordered the release of Shao Renmei, while Zhang Qian Shi and Chen Xianglong were kept in custody pending the appeal.

The Case of Xu Yan, Corrupt and Neglectful Water Patrol Squad Leader

Tried Yesterday by the Local Court

Involved in Four or Five Cases

Xu Yan, the dismissed leader of the Water Patrol Squad of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, was discovered by the former bureau chief Yuan Liang to have repeatedly committed acts of corruption and dereliction of duty. The bureau chief dispatched inspectors to seize the large quantity of opium that he had embezzled, and also arrested police officer Jiang Shihe, who was involved. Arrest warrants were issued for his accomplices, detectives Ma Zhiyun and Zhang Longfa. They were then handed over to the Local Court. The prosecutor arrested Zhang Xiaogou, the owner of a small goods store, and issued arrest warrants for Wu Qiaofu, Qin Genda, and Shen Liansheng, also owners of small goods stores and opium dealers. It is now known that Xu Yan, Jiang Shihe, Zhang Xiaogou and others have been formally indicted. Xu Yan is accused of four or five counts of corruption and malfeasance. At 10:00 AM yesterday, Judge Qian Chengjun opened the First Tribunal to hear the case.

Judge Xu Yan (questioned): Xu Yan, is Jiang Shihe your assistant? (Answer) I transferred him here. (Question) What about Zhang Xiaogou? He does business at the docks. (Question) What about Ma Zhiyun and Zhang Longfa? (Answer) Detectives. (Question) What about Wu Qiaofu? (Answer) The same business as Zhang Xiaogou. (Question) What about Li Yuting and Chen Jinshan? (Answer) Inspectors. (Question) What about Qin Genda and Shen Lian? (Answer) I haven't seen them. (Question) Is Qin Genda Ma Zhiyun's partner, and is Shen Liansheng a relative of Zhang Longfa? (Answer) I don't know. (Question) In September of last year, opium was discovered on the Dada Steamer. Who seized it? (Answer) I was on sick leave, so Vice-Captain Zi Menggan was in charge. The patrol police seized it. (Question) How much was seized? (Answer) I don't know. (Question) It was 195 packages, but how much was handed over? (Answer) 45 packages. When I recovered from my illness, I realized it was a big problem, but my first leave was reported in a letter on September 12th or 13th, and after the Fifth Congress, I submitted another request to extend my leave. (Question) It is said that Ma Zhiyun sold the opium. (Answer) I didn't know before, I only found out after going to court. (Question) Did you get any money? (Answer) No. (Question) You once said that you received 750 yuan. You can't deny that. (Answer) At that time, the duties were completely handled by Vice-Captain Dou. After I found out, I transferred Jiang Shihe to the team as an assistant to investigate. The jurisdiction of the Water Patrol Squad extends from Yangsi Bridge in the south to Yejidun in the west, and to the Wusong Estuary in the east. It comprises four divisions and eight police stations. Every opium case was solved. (Question) When did this happen? (Answer) It seems like around September 12th or 13th. At this point, the judge said, "This is the first case. Now we will ask about the second case." (Question) On October 5th, the Second Division seized 700 boxes of red pills. Who seized them? (Answer) I don't know. (Question) Who sent this to the headquarters? (Answer) At 6 PM that afternoon, I went to offer condolences because the mother of Yang Binxin, a member of the French Concession Municipal Council, had passed away. After I came back, I had a social engagement, and no one reported to me the next day. When the case was discovered, the bureau chief said that I sold the red pills and got more than 3,000 yuan. (Question) Was this 3,500 yuan also sold by Ma Zhiyun? (Answer) Yes. (Question) You admitted to receiving 1,700 yuan at the Public Security Bureau. (Answer) I didn't read the statement when the Public Security Bureau questioned me. I was forced to sign it. (Question) Why did you tear out a page from the case submission book? (Answer) If I were cheating, why wouldn't I burn it? The judge said, "Now we will ask about the third case." (Question) On the night of October 20th, 3,800 taels of opium were seized in the Huangpu River. Who seized it? (Answer) Patrol officers Jiang Zhende and a Mr. Wang seized it. (Question) Were the people transporting the opium Qin Genda and Shen Liansheng? When was the boatman Zhou Fucheng brought in? (Answer) It was already midnight. I found him asleep at home. (Question) Did a Lu Jinbao come to your house? (Answer) Only Jiang Shihe came to report to me, saying that he had recruited them. I called patrol officer Wang Shuxiu to ask him. I said, let's deal with it tomorrow. The next day, the officer on duty said that there was a big commotion in the team, so I went. (Question) Jiang Shihe released these opium dealers? (Answer) I only found out after going to court. (Question) Was Ma Zhiyun at your house when Jiang Shihe came? (Answer) No, I was already asleep. (Question) Did you get 1,300 yuan? (Answer) No. (Question) Is the opium still there? (Answer) Yes, but the two opium dealers are gone. (Question) Did you take money to release them? (Answer) If I were guilty, I wouldn't have turned myself in to the bureau. At this point, the questioning moved to the fourth and fifth cases. (Question) How much did the small goods stores offer you each month? (Answer) If I hadn't banned the small goods stores, this incident wouldn't have happened. (Question) You said earlier that Wu Qiaofu and Zhang Sheng sent you 300 yuan, and Zhang Xiaogou sent 400 yuan. (Answer) I didn't take it. It was Inspector Zhou Dehou who took it. I never met Zhang Xiaogou and the others. Then he said that he had never imagined that he would be transferred to the Water Patrol Squad. He was recommended by He Yingqin when he came to Shanghai because he had successfully negotiated the building of Hague Road in the Sixth District, Sixth Precinct, during his tenure, and the bureau chief thought he was capable. The previous captain resigned due to the kidnapping case of the "Shishi Xinbao" [China Times] manager, so I was transferred to be the captain. I have always been very dedicated to my duties. The judge said that this statement was irrelevant to the case and did not need to be recorded in the testimony. Xu Yan confirmed that this was because the person being questioned was not giving his testimony as fully as possible.

Jiang Shihe: The judge then questioned Jiang Shihe. (Question) When did you become an assistant in the Water Patrol Squad? (Answer) I am a fourth-class police officer, and the order to write was on September 12th. I was transferred from the Sixth District. (Question) Who transferred you? (Answer) I received an order from the Public Security Bureau. (Question) Who proposed it? (Answer) I don't know. (Answer) How much opium did patrolmen Jiang Zhende and others seize on October 20th? (Answer) Five bags. (Question) When did they seize it? (Answer) I don't know. I was already asleep at the time. The case-receiving patrolman reported it to patrol officer Wang Shuxiu, passing by my lodgings. (Question) When did you go to Xu Yan's place? (Answer) I went to his house around 2 or 3 AM to report to him. (Question) Was Ma Zhiyun there? (Answer) Yes, in Xu Yan's living room. I went to where he was sleeping. (Question) Did the opium dealers Qin Genda and Pai Liansheng leave on the captain's order? (Answer) No. (Question) You confessed at the Public Security Bureau that you released them on behalf of the captain. (Answer) The section chief scared me by saying that I would be tortured and forced me to say yes. (Question) Then who released them? (Answer) I don't know. (Question) How much money did you get? (Answer) None. I am a fourth-class police captain. If I wanted to release someone, I would just tell Officer Wang.

Zhang Xiaogou: The judge then questioned Zhang Xiaogou. (Question) What do you do? (Answer) A bargeman. (Question) Do you know Xu Yan? (Answer) I don't know him. (Question) Why did you give him 400 yuan? (Answer) I didn't. (Question) You are a small goods store owner? (Answer) No. (Question) If you don't know Xu Yan, why would he falsely accuse you? (Answer) There is no such thing. (Question) Why didn't you respond to the summons until you were arrested with a warrant? (Answer) If I had known, I would have surrendered myself earlier. At this point, the judge said that there were still many witnesses in the case who had not been summoned and adjourned the hearing to a later date to summon the witnesses and continue the trial. The defendants Xu Yan and Jiang Shihe were returned to custody, Zhang Xiaogou was released on bail, and the court adjourned.

Strange Drama of Two Families Fighting Over a Coffin

A Woman Married Twice and Had Two Sons with Each Husband

Fighting Over the Coffin After Death, Even Resorting to Violence

Resolved by Marrying a Deceased Wife to the First Husband

The deceased farmer Wang Changgen, who lived in Wangjiatang, west of Hongqiao Town in Shanghai, married Zhang, and had two sons, Yutang, now 32 years old and an employee of Yoyee Hong, and Songtang, 30 years old and working for a certain company. However, when Changgen died, they were both young. Due to financial difficulties, Zhang abandoned her two biological sons and remarried to Peng Axin, a carpenter in the vicinity. Yutang and Songtang were raised by Changgen's sister-in-law, Shen. After Zhang remarried, she also had two sons, Qingxiang, 27 years old, and Qingsheng, 25 years old, both of whom were married. The two brothers inherited their father's business, which has been doing well recently and they have accumulated some savings. Unexpectedly, after Axin died in the winter of the 16th year of the Republic [1927], the Wang brothers repeatedly went to the Peng family to persuade their mother to return home to fulfill her filial duty. However, Zhang vowed not to return and said, "After I die, you can carry my coffin back and bury it with your father Changgen. Although Qing and Qingsheng were born to a different father, they should be treated as family. Do not argue with each other to avoid resentment." Yutang and others, seeing that they could not persuade her, had to return home. Unexpectedly, on the 20th of last month, Zhang died suddenly from an illness. The coffin was temporarily placed next to Peng Axin's tomb, awaiting a propitious day for burial. After hearing the news, Yutang and the others were overcome with grief and immediately put on mourning clothes at home, observing the proper etiquette. They said, "Living in this world with a father but no mother is laughable," and on the night of the 6th of this month, they gathered a group of people and secretly stole Zhang's coffin back, hiding it in the woodshed and sending people to guard it day and night to prevent it from being stolen back. Later, when Qing heard about this, he was also unwilling to let it go. On the night before last (the 11th), he led a group of people to go in the snowy night. They were discovered by the guards who confronted them. Neither side would give way, resulting in a fight. As a result, Peng Qingxiang was injured and suffered two knife wounds to his leg and fell to the ground. The others dispersed. Seeing that he had caused trouble, Yutang hired someone to mediate the situation. It has now been settled. Peng Qingxiang is treating his injuries, and the Zhang coffin will be taken back by the Peng family for burial. In addition, a deceased wife (a virgin who died many years ago) will be married to Wang Changgen, with three days of chanting. All expenses will be borne by the Peng family. The drama of fighting over a coffin has now been peacefully resolved.

Reward Offered for the Arrest of the Perpetrator of a Filial Crime

Reward of 500 Yuan

Wanted: Li Shude

The Municipal Public Security Bureau issued a notice yesterday, stating that it was offering a reward for the arrest of a criminal. The notice stated that the complainant, Li Bolu, of Haiyan, a businessman in Shanghai residing at 3 Xingyou Lane, Zixia Road, outside the Dadongmen, had filed a report stating that his grandson, Shude, was a ne'er-do-well who loafed about. On the morning of January 3rd of this year, at around 10:00 AM, he and a friend dressed in military uniforms, wearing armed belts, speaking with a Hunan accent, and around 20 years old, whose name was unknown, came to the house together, claiming to have come to Shanghai from afar. They were invited to lunch. Later, the complainant and his daughter went out on business, leaving only his wife, Yao, Shude, and his friend at home. Unexpectedly, at around 5:00 PM in the evening, he returned home to find no one at home and a sense of unease. He searched everywhere and was horrified to find his wife, Yao, strangled with a rope and lying dead in the kitchen. Valuables were also stolen. There was no doubt that it was his grandson Shude and his friend who had conspired to kill and steal the property before fleeing. He immediately reported the incident to the First District Police Station for investigation, but without success. Later, the Shanghai Local Court sent officials to investigate and question the case. This case of murder for money is a tragic example of a filial crime. The circumstances are serious and shocking. If the criminal is allowed to escape the law for a long time, how can the national laws be upheld and public safety be maintained? Therefore, the complainant is attaching photographs of the criminal Li Shude and is earnestly requesting that the Bureau approve and issue a notice, offering a reward and ordering the subordinate detectives to intensify their search. If the criminal in this case can be apprehended and the facts confirmed, he is willing to provide a reward of 200 yuan for safekeeping, hoping to solve the case as soon as possible, punish the perpetrator according to the law, and comfort the departed soul. He is grateful both in life and in death. The complainant is submitting twenty photographs of the criminal Li Shude. Upon investigation, this case was previously reported by the First District, and since it is a filial crime with serious circumstances, it is no ordinary case of murder for money. An order has been issued to strictly investigate and arrest the criminal, and this Bureau has offered a reward of 300 yuan, ordering all subordinate police detectives to cooperate closely and arrest and bring the criminal to justice. Now, based on the previous report, the complainant is voluntarily offering an additional reward of 200 yuan to solve the case as soon as possible. Therefore, this notice is issued for public information. Regardless of who it is, anyone who can apprehend and deliver the fugitive Li Shude and his unknown Hunanese accomplice to the Bureau, or provide accurate information leading to their arrest, will be rewarded immediately upon confirmation of the facts, with the reward being held in reserve and never delayed. However, no one is allowed to make false accusations due to personal grudges, which would harm innocent people. Be careful! This notice is hereby issued.

Good News for Creditors of the Riye Bank

Yu Qiaqing's Responsible Response

The Provisional Committee of Creditors of the Savings Department of the Riye Bank Dàshìjiè (Great World) was anxious because the repayment period was approaching but there was no clear plan or date for settling the debts. Yesterday (the 13th), they again sent representatives, including Jing Xiren, Zuo Zhengping, Lu Bingyan, Cai Wenbin, Yuan Youlan, Tu Yunchao and others, to the Municipal Government and Yu, Wang, Wang, and Yuan to negotiate separately. The results were very satisfactory, and Yu's statement was particularly sincere, demonstrating a responsible attitude and expression. Details are as follows:

Yu Qiaqing's Statement: After the representatives of the Provisional Committee of Creditors presented the plight of the impoverished creditors and earnestly expressed that the majority of creditors firmly believed in the resolve and enthusiasm of the officials and the Municipal Government to protect the common people, they requested that a plan be promptly determined and the debts be repaid as soon as possible. Mr. Yu then gave a responsible response, stating that although the three had withdrawn from the Huang Resettlement Association, they still cared about the suffering of the majority of the common people and would continue to earnestly consult with Mr. Wang, Mr. Wang, and Mr. Yuan to seek a guarantee plan from the Municipal Government. Although progress had been hindered by various disputes, he would always be responsible for maintaining the situation. Currently, regarding the issue of the French Court lawsuit, it had been decided that Mayor Zhang would hire Wu Jingxiong, Chen Ting Shuo, and Qin Liankui as pro bono lawyers to represent the Municipal Government and the 10,000+ creditors who had registered with both Xu Yongzuo and the Provisional Committee of Creditors to file a lawsuit in the French Court for legal redress and then fundamentally resolve the situation to ensure that the creditors would not suffer losses and the repayment time would not be extended. The resolution plan would be divided into: (1) liquidating the five business operations of the Gongfa Company; (2) liquidating Huang's personal property; (3) requiring the directors of the Gongfa Company to assume unlimited liability; (4) the Municipal Government would be responsible for finding a way to maintain the situation. As for the source of funds, it had been determined early on: (1) the Chinese-Western Pharmacy was valued at 200,000; (2) the Hot Spring Bathhouse was valued at 50,000; (3) the Fuchang Tobacco Company was valued at 1.3 million, with 500,000 to be handed over first; (4) Huang's personal property would be handed over with 400,000 first; (5) the Dàshìjiè (Great World) was assumed to be worth over a million, and would be handled by the Municipal Government for further determination. All plans would have a practical solution announced no later than next Monday, and he would be responsible regardless of the outcome. He hoped that all creditors would not cause more disputes due to impatience, and especially that savings passbooks and deposit slips should not be sold at a discount due to incitement, which could lead to unexpected losses. The representatives were satisfied and expressed their gratitude before departing.

The Municipal Government's Statement: The representatives presented their business cards to see Mayor Zhang. As a municipal meeting was in progress, a representative was sent to receive them, accept their petition, and respond on behalf of the mayor, stating that the mayor was discussing a practical solution with Mr. Yu and others and would announce it to the public as soon as possible.

Yuan Ludeng's Remarks: Mr. Yuan stated that there had not been much concrete progress in recent days due to various twists and turns. He has always prioritized the interests of the public, but his position is more difficult. However, he would fully respect Mr. Yu's suggestions to ensure that the entire debt was not lost. As far as his personal burden was concerned, as long as he was capable, he would gladly comply.

Public Concession Bureau Streamlines Traffic on Nanjing Road

Implementation Begins on March 9th

The Public Concession Bureau is amending Article 48 of the traffic regulations due to increased traffic on Nanjing Road. The regulations now state that no vehicles of any kind may be parked on the road for more than thirty minutes. These measures will take effect on March 9th. The amended regulations are as follows: No vehicles of any kind may be parked on Nanjing Road for more than thirty minutes between 8:00 AM and 6:00 PM daily. The locations where parking is permitted during these times will be marked with white-painted curb stones. Locations with red-painted curb stones will be prohibited from parking at any time. No parking is allowed on the north side of Nanjing Road from 8:00 AM to 9:30 AM and from 1:30 PM to 2:30 PM. No parking is allowed on the south side of Nanjing Road from 11:30 AM to 12:30 PM and from 4:00 PM to 6:00 PM.

Chinese Benevolent Child Welfare Association Invites Dr. Hu Xu Peng to Lecture

Child Training in the Family

American educator Dr. Hu Xu Peng, the creator of the "Winnetka Plan," has arrived in Shanghai and is being warmly welcomed by all parties. The "Winnetka Plan" includes four important principles: (1) to enable children to acquire as much knowledge and skills as possible for future life; (2) to enable each child to enjoy childhood life naturally, happily, and perfectly; (3) human progress relies on the full development of each individual; (4) the welfare of the community must have the development of a complete social meaning among all its members. It has profound significance in child welfare work. The Chinese Benevolent Child Welfare Association has always been enthusiastic about promoting parental education. It has specially arranged to host a reception for Dr. Hu on Sunday (the 15th) at 12 noon at the Hong Kong Road Bankers' Association, and will invite Dr. Hu to deliver a lecture on "Child Training in the Family." In addition to the association's committee members and staff, several child education experts will be present. Those who wish to attend the gathering can contact the association in advance at No. 20 Museum Road.

The Shanghai-Jiading line (i.e., the Shanghai-Jiading line) of the Zhabei Shanghai-Taicang Long-Distance Bus Company, which passes through Shiyifen Guhang, Changbang Bridge, Luodian, Shi Xianggong Temple, and Xinjing Bridge to Jiading, has more than ten trips back and forth every day, and is very crowded with passengers. Page 16

The company announced the suspension of service yesterday afternoon. Chronicle of Early Spring Rain and Snow

The city has experienced continuous rain and snow in recent days, and various commercial and transportation organizations have suffered losses. The weather did not clear up until yesterday. In the morning, there was continuous rain. At 4:30 in the afternoon, snow pellets suddenly fell, followed by light rain. At 5:50, snow pellets fell again, as large as yellow beans and as small as mung beans. When they fell, the sound on the glass doors and windows was crisp and clear. After about twenty minutes, the flower sheds in the surrounding countryside were damaged. Then, the continuous spring rain was as greasy and suffocating as ointment.

Lu Yifang Still Fined 300 Yuan

Lu Yifang, the editor of the "Ling Bao" tri-weekly, was sued in a criminal self-accusation to the Shanghai Special District Court by movie star Hu Die for publishing an article about the Snow Butterfly marriage, claiming the article was libelous. The court found the facts to be true and sentenced Lu Yifang to a fine of 300 yuan and ordered him to deposit 500 yuan as bail. Lu was not satisfied and hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to file an appeal. On the afternoon of the 6th of this month, President Zhou Hanting, together with Judges Cheng and Xiao, summoned Lu, who was accompanied by lawyers Jiang Yiping and Zhang Chongding, to court to state the reasons for the appeal. The appellant, Hu Die, still hired lawyer Zhan Jifeng to appear in court as her representative. After President Zhou questioned the witnesses in detail, the lawyers for both parties engaged in fierce debate. The court announced the end of the debate and scheduled the sentencing for the afternoon of the 13th of this month. Yesterday was the sentencing date. The appellant, Lu Yifang, accompanied by his lawyers Jiang Yiping and Zhang Chongding, came to court to await the verdict. The appellant, Hu Die, was not present and was represented by lawyer Zhan. At 2:30, President Zhou took the seat in the First Criminal Court and announced the verdict. The main text of the original judgment, except for the part concerning the commutation of punishment, was reversed. Lu Yifang was sentenced to a fine of 300 yuan for the crime of disseminating words that damaged the reputation of others, and the original bail of 500 yuan was still required.

Investigation of Two Extortion Gangs

Yun Tieqiao and Others Were Extorted

Guns, Bullets, and Stamps Were Seized

Chen Junbao, who lives at No. 197 Moore Road, received two threatening letters last month demanding 5,000 yuan. He reported this to the Jing'an Temple Police Station, which sent detectives Wang Zhusheng and Shan Huihai to arrest Zhou Wangzuo, a native of Shaoxing, at a Chinese-Western teahouse on Edward Road. The day before yesterday afternoon, another accomplice, Zhang Jinhai (aka Yong Sheng), a native of Suzhou, was arrested at the Pin Fang Teahouse on Guangdong Road. They confessed that the items they needed were placed in the Dongxing Inn on Lafei Road in the French Concession. When they went to search, they found a rattan box containing seven bullets, many envelopes and stationery, and various stamps. After investigation, it was learned that Zhou and Zhang had extorted large sums of money from doctors Shen Zhuoru and Yun Tieqiao on Gu Ling Road and Yunnan Road from December 1928 to May 1929. Shen Yuruo was also extorted 200 yuan. Wang Gaosheng and Tian Yushu, although they sent letters demanding 3,000 and 2,000 yuan respectively, did not receive any money in the end. Yesterday morning, it was rumored that the victims had taken the two bandits to the Special District Court, where Judge Ge interrogated them. Police lawyer Wang Tang presented the seized items as evidence, briefly described the process, and requested that another hearing be scheduled. Zhou Wangzuo confessed that Zhang was an accomplice. Zhang also admitted that he, Zhou, and a Tan surnamed person who was on the run, discussed extorting the Chen family in a smoking den in the French Concession a month ago. The letter was written by him and sent by Tan. He also admitted to extorting 150 yuan from Yun Tieqiao. The court ordered the two defendants to be remanded in custody and adjourned the hearing.

Nine-Cheng Gold Mixed with Counterfeit City Brand Goods

The Shanghai Goldsmiths' Association (i.e., Da Tong Hang), including Yang Qinghe, Lao Qingyun, Fengxiang, Jingfu, Qiu Tianbao, Fei Wenyuan, Bao Cheng, Fang Jiuxia, and other gold shops, has discovered that nine-cheng gold bracelets have been found on the market recently, mixed with counterfeit materials and bearing counterfeit seals of various gold shops in order to deceive and defraud. Young Man Dies Tragically on Ferry

Determined to be Caused by Poisoning

Whether There are Family Members is Unknown

Yesterday morning at 8:15, the Taikoo Company's fast Da Ban Tou small ferry was about to return to Pudong at the French Company's wharf, when a nameless young man with a pale face was helped onto the ferry to cross to Pudong by a Mr. Jia, a hotel employee from the Xiangbin Hotel on Sima Road. After the matter was completed, Mr. Jia returned to shore, and the ferry immediately returned to Pudong. Unexpectedly, just as the ferry arrived in Pudong, the young man suddenly fell down and died. Zhao Shengsheng, the captain of the ferry, saw the situation and was unable to provide immediate assistance, so he returned the ferry to its original location and reported the incident to the Water Patrol Police and the French Concession Police. Soon, the French Municipal Council arrived by car and transported the deceased to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall for temporary burial, pending investigation and identification. It is reported that the deceased was about 20 years old, wearing a blue cloth jacket and trousers, a peaked cap, and broken shoes. His name is unknown. Judging from his appearance, he seemed to be a crew member. He had a packet of cloth medicine powder and several copper coins on his person. Observers unanimously determined that he had committed suicide by poisoning, but the cause of his death is still difficult to determine at this time. According to the hotel employee, Mr. Jia, the deceased called him to help him board the ferry when he was not dead at the dock. The deceased claimed that he lived in Zhangjiayan, Pudong, and so on. Whether there are family members to identify him will be investigated later.
